$$\mathbf{Z}_{\tau} = [\mathbf{s} \mid \mathbf{I}_{\rho}] \cdot \begin{bmatrix} a_{\tau} \\ \mathbf{b}_{\tau} \end{bmatrix} \cdot \mathbf{v}^{\mathsf{T}} \in \mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\rho \times \rho},$$

where  $\mathbf{I}_{\rho} \in \mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\rho \times \rho}$  is the identity matrix. Namely, the components of  $p\mathbf{k}$  consist of  $g^{\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}}$  for all  $\tau \in [T]$ . Since  $t_i \neq s_i c \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$ , by the Chinese remainder theorem, it must be the case that  $t_i \neq s_i c \pmod{p'}$  or  $t_i \neq s_i c \pmod{q'}$ . Without loss of generality, suppose that  $t_i \neq s_i c \pmod{p'}$ . In this case the vector  $[t_i \mid c \cdot \mathbf{e}_i]$  is linearly independent of the rows of the matrix  $[\mathbf{s} \pmod{p'} \mid \mathbf{I}_{\rho}]$ . Since  $a_{\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{b}_{\tau}$  are uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}$ , the components  $a_{\tau} \mod p'$  and  $\mathbf{b}_{\tau} \mod p'$  are uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'}$ . By linear independence over  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'}$ , the value of  $a_{\tau}t_i + b_{\tau,i}c \pmod{p'}$  is uniformly random over  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'}$  even given  $\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}$  for all  $\tau \in [T]$ . As such, the conditional min-entropy of the vector  $\boldsymbol{\omega}_i$  from Eq. (D.3) is at least  $T \log p' > T$ . By an analogous argument as in the previous case, we can now appeal to Lemma 2.6 and conclude that the output distribution of  $H(\boldsymbol{\omega}_i)$  is statistically close to uniform over  $\{0,1\}^{\lambda}$ , in which case the probability that  $u_i = H(\boldsymbol{\omega}_i)$  is negligible.

• The only remaining case is when  $\hat{c} = 0 = \hat{t}_i$ ,  $t_i = s_i c$ , and  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{t_i}, g^{t_i}h)$ . In this case,  $(g^{t_i})^{a_{\tau}}(g^c)^{b_{\tau,i}} = g^{(a_{\tau}s_i + b_{\tau,i})c}$  for all  $\tau \in [T]$ . Since  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}$ , with overwhelming probability, there will be some component that is invertible modulo p'q'. If so, there always exists  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  such that  $\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v} = c$ . Then, in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$ , the challenger outputs 1 if and only if

$$u_i = H(g^{(a_1s_i+b_{1,i})c}, \dots, g^{(a_Ts_i+b_{T,i})c}) = H(g^{(a_1s_i+b_{1,i})\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}, \dots, g^{(a_Ts_i+b_{T,i})\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v})$$
$$= H(g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{z}_1, \dots, g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{z}_T),$$

where  $\mathbf{z}_{\tau,i} = (a_{\tau}s_i + b_{\tau,i})\mathbf{v}$  are the components in the public key. This is precisely the verification relation in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j}$ .

In each case, we see that the  $j^{\text{th}}$  call to Verify is implemented correctly with overwhelming probability in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j}$ .

To complete the proof, it suffices to show that for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , the output of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2(\mathcal{A})$  is 0 with overwhelming probability. Let  $(\sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*)$  be the adversary's output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ . The output of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$  is 1 only if  $\mathsf{Verify}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{sk}, \sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*) = 1$  and  $r_{i^*} \neq r^*$  where  $r \leftarrow \mathsf{Open}(\mathsf{crs}, \sigma^*)$ . Write  $\sigma^* = g^c h^{\hat{c}}$  and  $\pi^* = (g^{t_{i^*}} h^{\hat{t}_{i^*}}, u_{i^*})$  In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ , if  $\mathsf{Verify}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{sk}, \sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*) = 1$ , it must be the case that  $\hat{c} = 0$ ,  $\hat{t}_{i^*} = 0$ ,  $t_{i^*} = s_{i^*} c$ , and

$$r^* = \mathsf{LEQ}\big(g^{t_{i^*}}h^{\hat{t}_{i^*}}, g^{t_{i^*}}h^{\hat{t}_{i^*}+1}\big) = \mathsf{LEQ}\big(g^{s_{i^*}c}, g^{s_{i^*}c}h\big).$$

Moreover, since  $\hat{c} = 0$ ,  $r_{i^*} = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{cs_{i^*}}, g^{cs_{i^*}}h) = r^*$ . In this case, the output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$  is 0, and the theorem follows.

**Proof of Theorem 5.8 (Statistical Simulation).** We construct a simulator  $S = (S_1, S_2)$  as follows:

•  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}) \to (\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{pk}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{sk}})$ : Sample  $(N, p, q) \leftarrow \operatorname{SampleModulus}(1^{\lambda})$ , where p = 2p' + 1 and q = 2q' + 1. Let g be a generator of  $\mathbb{QR}_N$  and h = -1. Sample a vector  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}$ , scalars  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\rho} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}$ , and a hash function  $H \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{H}$ . Set  $\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \ldots, g^{s_{\rho} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\rho}})$ . Sample  $a_{\tau}, b_{\tau, i} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}$  for all  $\tau \in [T]$  and  $i \in [\rho]$ . Output  $\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}$ ,  $\widetilde{\operatorname{pk}} = \{g^{(a_{\tau}s_i + b_{\tau, i})\mathbf{v}} h^{a_{\tau}\mathbf{e}_i}\}_{\tau \in [T], i \in [\rho]}$ ,  $\widetilde{\operatorname{sk}} = \{a_{\tau}, b_{\tau, i}\}_{\tau \in [T], i \in [\rho]}$ , and  $\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{pk}}, p', q', s_1, \ldots, s_{\rho})$ .

•  $S_2(\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, I, r_I) \to (\widetilde{\sigma}, \{\widetilde{\pi}_i\}_{i \in I})$ : On input  $\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{pk}}, p', q', s_1, \dots, s_{\varrho})$  where

$$\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = \left(N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_\rho \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_\rho}\right) \quad \text{and} \quad \widetilde{\mathsf{pk}} = \{g^{\mathbf{z}_{\tau, i}} h^{\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau, i}}\}_{\tau \in [T], i \in [\rho]},$$

a set of indices  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , and a bitstring  $r_I \in \{0,1\}^{|I|}$ , the simulator samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{p'q'}$ . Then, for each  $i \in [\rho]$ , it samples  $\hat{y}'_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  as follows:

- If  $i \notin I$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$ .
- If  $i \in I$ , set  $\hat{y}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  to be the unique value where  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}_i}, g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}_i+1})$ .

Define  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\rho}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y'} \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{2}$ . The simulator then sets  $q^{t_i}q^{\hat{t}_i} = q^{s_i\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}_i}$  and

$$u_i = H(g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{z}_{1,i}}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{1,i}}, \dots, g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{z}_{T,i}}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{T,i}}).$$

Output  $\widetilde{\sigma} = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$  and  $\{\widetilde{\pi}_i\}_{i\in I}$  where  $\widetilde{\pi}_i = (g^{t_i}h^{\widehat{t}_i}, u_i)$ .

To show that  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 0]$  and  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 1]$  are statistically indistinguishable, we use a hybrid argument:

• Hyb<sub>0</sub>: This is the experiment ExptHide[ $\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 0$ ]. Namely, the challenger begins by sampling crs  $\leftarrow$  Setup( $1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}$ , hiding) and (pk, sk)  $\leftarrow$  KeyGen(crs). For each challenge query, the challenger first samples  $(\sigma, r, \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [\rho]}) \leftarrow$  GenBits(crs) and gives r to  $\mathcal{A}$  before receiving a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$  chosen by  $\mathcal{A}$ . It then replies with  $\sigma$  and  $\{\pi_i\}_{i \in I}$ .

More precisely, in this experiment,

$$\mathsf{crs} = \left(N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_\rho \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_\rho}\right) \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{pk} = \{g^{\mathbf{z}_{\tau, i}} h^{\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau, i}}\}_{\tau \in [T], i \in [\rho]},$$

where  $\mathbf{z}_{\tau,i} = (a_{\tau}s_i + b_{\tau,i})\mathbf{v}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i} = a_{\tau}\mathbf{e}_i$ . On each challenge query, the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{|N/2|}$  and computes

$$\sigma = q^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$$
 and  $q^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i} = q^{s_i\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{e}_i}$  and  $q^{u_{\tau,i}}h^{\hat{u}_{\tau,i}} = q^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{z}_{\tau,i}}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i}}$ ,

for all  $\tau \in [T]$  and  $i \in [\rho]$ . The random bits  $r_i$  satisfy  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i}, g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i+1})$ . Finally, the proofs  $\pi_i$  are given by  $\pi_i = (g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i}, u_i)$ , where  $u_i = H(g^{u_{1,i}}h^{\hat{u}_{1,i}}, \dots, g^{u_{T,i}}h^{\hat{u}_{T,i}})$ .

- $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$ : Same as  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$ , except that the challenger computes  $(\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{sk}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_1(1^\lambda, 1^\rho)$  and uses  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathrm{and} \widetilde{\mathsf{sk}}$  instead of  $\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{pk}, \mathrm{and} \mathsf{sk}$ , respectively.
- Hyb<sub>2</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>1</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{2p'q'}$  instead of  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{|N/2|}$ .
- Hyb<sub>3</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>2</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{y}} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{2}^{\rho}$ . It defines  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\rho}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{2}$ .

- Hyb<sub>4</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>3</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ . Then it samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$ . For each  $i \in [\rho]$ , it sets  $\hat{y}'_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  to be the unique value where  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}'_i}, g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}'_i+1})$ . Finally it sets  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\rho}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{2}$ . The remaining components are constructed as before.
- Hyb<sub>5</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>4</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\rho}$  after it receives the challenge set. In particular, on each query, after the challenger receives the set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , it sets  $\hat{y}'_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  to the unique value where  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}'_i}, g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}'_i+1})$  if  $i \in I$ , and otherwise, it samples  $\hat{y}'_i \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$ . All remaining components are constructed as in Hyb<sub>4</sub>. This is the distribution in ExptHide[ $\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 1$ ].

For an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ , we write  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i(\mathcal{A})$  to denote the output distribution of an execution of experiment  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i$  with adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ . We now show that the output distribution of each adjacent pair of hybrid experiments is statistically indistinguishable.

**Lemma D.4.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_1(A)$ .

*Proof.* Since  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$  samples  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}$ , and  $\widetilde{\mathsf{sk}}$  using the same procedure as Setup and KeyGen, the output distributions of hybrids  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$  are identically distributed.

<span id="page-60-0"></span>**Lemma D.5.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1(A) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_2(A)$ .

*Proof.* The only difference between  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$  is that the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y}$  uniformly at random from  $\mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{2p'q'}$  instead of  $\mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}$  when answering challenge queries. Since the distributions  $\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor})$  and  $\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'})$  are statistically indistinguishable (see Eq. (D.1)), the claim follows by a union bound (since  $\rho = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and  $\mathcal{A}$  makes a polynomial number of queries).

<span id="page-60-1"></span>**Lemma D.6.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_3(A)$ .

*Proof.* The two distribution only differ in how  $\mathbf{y}$  is sampled. In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{y}$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\rho}$  while in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ , we sample  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2^{\rho}$  and define  $\mathbf{y}$  so that  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{2}$ . These distributions are identical by the Chinese remainder theorem (since  $\gcd(p'q', 2) = 1$ ).

<span id="page-60-2"></span>Lemma D.7. For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_4(A)$ .

*Proof.* First,  $\mathbf{y}'$  is sampled identically in the two distributions. It suffices to show that once we fix  $\mathbf{y}'$ , there is a one-to-one correspondence between the value of  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\rho}$  and the value of r. Since g generates a subgroup of order p'q', and  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$ , we have that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ ,  $g^{s_i\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}} = g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$ . Similarly, since h has order 2,  $h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{e}_i} = h^{y_i} = h^{\hat{y}_i'}$ . This means that the bit  $r_i$  satisfies

$$r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i}, g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i+1}) = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}_i'}, g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}_i'+1}).$$

By construction of LEQ and the fact that h generates a subgroup of order 2, this means that

$$\mathsf{LEQ}(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{(1-\hat{y}_i')}, g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{(1-\hat{y}_i')+1}) = 1 - \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}_i'}, g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}_i'+1}) = 1 - r_i,$$

and so we see that there is a one-to-one correspondence between  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\rho}$  and the bitstring  $r \in \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ . Both  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  enforce this correspondence, and thus, are identically distributed.

**Lemma D.8.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_5(A)$ .

*Proof.* First, the challenger generates the common reference string crs and the public key pk identically in the two experiments. It suffices to argue that the challenger's response to the adversary's challenge query is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ . In particular, on each challenge query, after the adversary outputs a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , the challenger replies with a commitment  $\sigma = g^{\mathsf{y^Tv}}$  and a collection of proofs  $\{\pi_i\}_{i\in I}$  where  $\pi_i = (g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i}, u_i)$ . We show that the commitment  $\sigma$  and the components  $t_i$ ,  $\hat{t}_i$ , and  $u_i$  are identically distributed in the two experiments:

- In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ , the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$ . Since g generates a subgroup of order p'q' and  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$ , it follows that  $\sigma = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}} = g^{(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$ , and so  $\sigma$  is identically distributed in the two experiments.
- In Hyb<sub>4</sub> and Hyb<sub>5</sub>, for all  $i \in I$ , the challenger samples  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$  conditioned on  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}_i}, g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}_i+1})$ . Thus, the variables  $\hat{y}'_i$  for  $i \in I$  in the two experiments are identically distributed. In both experiments, it then defines

<span id="page-61-1"></span>
$$g^{t_i}g^{\hat{t}_i} = g^{s_i\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{e}_i = g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}'_i},$$

and so all of the  $g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i}$  terms for  $i \in I$  are identically distributed.

• In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ ,  $u_i = H(g^{u_{1,i}}h^{\hat{u}_{1,i}}, \dots, g^{u_{T,i}}h^{\hat{u}_{T,i}})$  where

$$g^{u_{\tau,i}}h^{\hat{u}_{\tau,i}} = g^{\mathbf{y}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{z}_{\tau,i}}h^{\mathbf{y}^{\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i}} = g^{(\mathbf{y}')^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{z}_{\tau,i}}h^{a_{\tau}\hat{y}'_{i}}, \tag{D.4}$$

using the fact that g generates a group of order p'q', h generates a group of order 2 and  $\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i} = a_{\tau}\mathbf{e}_i$ . Since all of the components in Eq. (D.4) are identically distributed for all  $i \in I$  and  $\tau \in [T]$ , we conclude that the components  $u_i$  for  $i \in I$  are also identically distributed.  $\square$ 

Theorem 5.8 now follows by a hybrid argument.

## <span id="page-61-0"></span>D.2 Analysis of Construction 5.9 (Dual-Mode (Malicious) HBG from QR)

In this section, we give the proofs for the correctness and security theorems (Theorems 5.10 to 5.14) for the dual-mode hidden-bits generator with malicious security from QR (Construction 5.9). The analysis proceeds very similarly to that of the basic QR scheme (Construction 5.3) in Appendix D.1.

**Proof of Theorem 5.10 (Correctness).** Follows by an analogous argument as the proof of Theorem 5.4.

**Proof of Theorem 5.11 (Succinctness).** The commitment  $\sigma$  in Construction 5.9 consists of a PRG seed  $s \in \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  where  $\kappa = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and an element of  $\mathbb{Z}_N$ , which has size  $2 \lceil \log N \rceil = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ . Thus,  $|\sigma| = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ .

**Proof of Theorem 5.12 (CRS Indistinguishability).** Same as the proof of Theorem 5.6.  $\Box$ 

**Proof of Theorem 5.13 (Statistical Binding).** Follows by a similar argument as in the proof of Theorem 5.7. Specifically, we first show that we can substitute the real verification algorithm Verify with the following algorithm. On input  $(\sigma, i, r_i, \pi_i)$ , the challenger does the following:

- Write  $\sigma = (s, \overline{c})$  and  $\pi_i = \{(j, \overline{t}_j, u_j)\}_{j \in S}$  for an implicitly defined set S. Let  $(\hat{S}_1, \dots, \hat{S}_\rho, \boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(s)$ , and define the shifted set  $S_i \leftarrow \{j + \ell \cdot (i-1) \mid j \in \hat{S}_i\}$ . If  $S \neq S_i$ , output 0.
- If  $\bar{c} \neq g^c$  for some  $c \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$ , output 0.
- If  $\bar{t}_j \neq g^{cs_j}$  for any  $j \in S_i$ , output 0. Here,  $s_j \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  is sampled by Setup and used to construct  $\operatorname{crs} = (N, g, h, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1\mathbf{v}}, \dots, g^{s_{\ell'}\mathbf{v}})$
- Compute  $\overline{t}_i' \leftarrow \prod_{j \in S_i} \overline{t}_j^{\alpha_j}$  and output 0 if  $r_i \neq \mathsf{LEQ}(\overline{t}_i', \overline{t}_i'h)$ .
- Take any  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$  such that  $\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v} = c$ , and write the public key as  $\mathsf{pk} = \{g^{\mathbf{z}_{\tau,i}}\}_{\tau \in [T], i \in [\ell']}$ . If  $u_j \neq H(g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{z}_{1,j}}, \dots, g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{z}_{T,j}})$  for some  $j \in S_i$ , or if no such  $\mathbf{y}$  exists, then output 0. If all checks pass, output 1.

Using the same argument as the proof of Theorem 5.7 (applied to each individual component  $\sigma$ ,  $\bar{t}_j$ , and  $u_j$ ), and appealing to a union bound, we can conclude that the output of the real verification algorithm and this modified verification algorithm are identical with overwhelming probability. Similarly, as in the proof of Theorem 5.7, no adversary is able to win the binding game with respect to the modified verification algorithm, and the claim follows.

**Proof of Theorem 5.14 (Statistical Hiding).** We construct a simulator  $S = (S_1, S_2)$  as follows:

•  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}) \to (\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{crs}})$ : Sample  $(N, p, q) \leftarrow \operatorname{\mathsf{SampleModulus}}(1^{\lambda})$ , where p = 2p' + 1 and q = 2q' + 1. Let g be a generator of  $\mathbb{QR}_N$  and h = -1 be the generator of  $\mathbb{H} = \{\pm 1\}$ . Sample a vector  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\ell'}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}$ , scalars  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\ell'} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}$ , and a hash function  $H \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{H}$ . Output

$$\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = \left(N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_{\ell'} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\ell'}}\right).$$

and  $\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}, p', q', s_1, \dots, s_{\ell'}).$ 

•  $S_2(\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}},\mathsf{pk},I,r_I) \to (\widetilde{\sigma},\{\widetilde{\pi}_i\}_{i\in I})$ : On input  $\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}},p',q',s_1,\ldots,s_{\ell'})$  where

$$\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = \left(N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_{\ell'} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\ell'}}\right),$$

a public key  $\mathsf{pk} = \{\overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i}\}_{\tau \in [T], i \in [\ell']}$ , a set of indices  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , and a bitstring  $r_I \in \{0,1\}^{|I|}$ , the simulator does the following:

- 1. Check that  $\overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i} \in \mathbb{J}_N^{\ell'}$  for all  $\tau \in [T]$  and  $i \in [\ell']$ . Output  $\bot$  if this is not the case.
- 2. Sample a seed  $\mathbf{s} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  and compute  $(\hat{S}_1,\ldots,\hat{S}_{\rho},\boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(\mathbf{s})$ , where  $\boldsymbol{\alpha} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\rho\ell}$ . For each  $i \in I$ , it computes the shifted sets  $S_i \leftarrow \{j + \ell \cdot (i-1) \mid j \in \hat{S}_i\}$ .
- 3. Sample  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$ . Then, it samples a vector  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell'}$  as follows:
  - For each  $i \in I$ , let  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$ . Then, set  $\hat{\omega}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  to be the unique value where  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{\omega}_i}, g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{\omega}_i+1})$  Them, for each  $j \in S_i$  sample  $\hat{y}_j' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}_j' = \hat{\omega}_i$ .

- For all of the remaining indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$ . Define  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{2n'q'}^{\ell'}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{2}$ .
- 4. Next, the simulator computes  $\widetilde{\sigma} = (\mathbf{s}, g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}})$  and  $\overline{t}_j = g^{s_j\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{e}_j}$  for each  $j \in S_i$ . Next, for each  $j \in S_i$  and  $\tau \in [T]$ , compute  $\overline{u}_{\tau,j} \leftarrow \prod_{k \in [\ell']} \overline{z}_{\tau,j,k}^{y_k}$ , and set  $u_j \leftarrow H(\overline{u}_{1,j}, \dots, \overline{u}_{T,j})$ . It sets  $\widetilde{\pi}_i = \{(j, \overline{t}_i, u_j)\}_{j \in S_i}$ .
- 5. Output  $\widetilde{\sigma}$  and  $\{\widetilde{\pi}_i\}_{i\in I}$ .

We now use a hybrid argument to show that  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A},0]$  and  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A},1]$  are statistically indistinguishable:

- Hyb<sub>0</sub>: This is the experiment ExptHide[ $\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 0$ ]. Namely, the challenger begins by sampling crs  $\leftarrow$  Setup( $1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}$ , hiding), and gives crs to  $\mathcal{A}$ . The adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  replies with a public key pk. For each challenge query, the challenger samples  $(\sigma, r, \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [\rho]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{GenBits}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{pk})$  and gives r to  $\mathcal{A}$  before receiving a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$  chosen by  $\mathcal{A}$ . It then replies with  $\sigma$  and  $\{\pi_i\}_{i \in I}$ .
- $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$ : This experiment is identical to  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$ , except that the challenger computes  $(\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$  and uses  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$  in place of  $\mathsf{crs}$ . Everything else proceeds identically to  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$ .

Specifically, in this experiment, the challenger samples (N, p, q), H,  $\mathbf{v}$ ,  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\ell'}$  as specified by  $\mathcal{S}_1$  and sets  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \ldots, g^{s_{\ell'} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\ell'}})$ . It gives  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$  to  $\mathcal{A}$  to receive a public key  $\mathsf{pk} = \{\overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i}\}_{\tau \in [T], i \in [\ell']}$ . On a challenge query, the challenger proceeds as follows:

- 1. Check that  $\overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,i} \in \mathbb{J}_N^{\ell'}$  for all  $\tau \in [T]$  and  $i \in [\ell']$ , and output  $\bot$  otherwise.
- 2. Sample  $s \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  and compute  $(\hat{S}_1,\ldots,\hat{S}_{\rho},\boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(s)$ . For each  $i \in [\rho]$ , let  $S_i \leftarrow \{j+\ell\cdot(i-1) \mid j\in\hat{S}_i\}$ .
- 3. Sample  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}^{\ell'}$  and compute for each  $j \in [\ell']$  and  $\tau \in [T]$ ,

$$\overline{c} \leftarrow g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{t}_j \leftarrow g^{s_j\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{e}_j} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{u}_{\tau,j} \leftarrow \prod_{k \in [\ell']} (\overline{z}_{\tau,j,k})^{y_k}.$$

Then, for each  $j \in [\ell']$ , compute  $u_j \leftarrow H(\overline{u}_{1,j}, \dots, \overline{u}_{T,j})$ .

- 4. For each  $i \in [\rho]$ , compute  $\overline{t}_i' \leftarrow \prod_{j \in S_i} \overline{t}_j^{\alpha_j}$  and  $r_i \leftarrow \mathsf{LEQ}(\overline{t}_i', \overline{t}_i'h)$  and  $\pi_i \leftarrow \{(j, \overline{t}_j, u_j)\}_{j \in S_i}$ .
- 5. The challenger gives r to  $\mathcal{A}$  and receives a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ .
- 6. The challenger replies with  $\sigma=(\mathsf{s},\overline{c})$  and the set  $\{\pi_i\}_{i\in I}$ .
- $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ : Same as  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$ , except when responding to challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\ell'}$  instead of  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N/2 \rfloor}^{\ell'}$ .
- $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ : Same as  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ , except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell'}$ . It defines  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{2p'q'}^{\ell'}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{2}$ .
- Hyb<sub>4</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>3</sub>, except when responding to challenge queries, the challenger samples s and  $\mathbf{y}'$  as in Hyb<sub>3</sub>. Next, for each  $i \in [\rho]$ , it samples  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$ , and for  $j \in S_i$ , it samples  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}'_j = \hat{\omega}_i$ . For all of the remaining indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$ .

- Hyb<sub>5</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>4</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ . Then, after sampling **s** and **y**', it computes for each  $i \in [\rho]$ ,  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$ . Then, it sets  $\hat{\omega}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  to be the unique value where  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\omega}_i}, g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\omega}_i+1})$ .
- Hyb<sub>6</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>5</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell'}$  after it receives the challenge set. On each query, after the challenger receives the set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , for each  $i \in I$ , it samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}'$  as follows:
  - For each  $i \in I$ , let  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$ . Then, set  $\hat{\omega}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  to be the unique value where  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\omega}_i}, g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\omega}_i+1})$  Finally, sample  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$  for each  $j \in S_i$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}'_j = \hat{\omega}_i$ .
  - For all of the remaining indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$ .

The remaining components are constructed as in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ . This is exactly the distribution in  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 1]$ .

For an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ , we write  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i(\mathcal{A})$  to denote the output of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i(\mathcal{A})$  with adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ . In the following, we show that the output distribution on each pair of adjacent experiments is statistically indistinguishable (or identically distributed). Because  $\mathbb{H} = \{\pm 1\}$  is small, our analysis will rely on a stronger version of Claim C.11:

<span id="page-64-0"></span>Claim D.9. Suppose G is a secure PRG and take  $s \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$ . Let  $(\hat{S}_1,\ldots,\hat{S}_{\rho},\boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(s)$ . Then, with overwhelming probability over the choice of s, the following properties hold:

- For any  $i \in [\rho]$ ,  $\Pr[\exists j \in \hat{S}_i : \alpha_j \neq 0] = 1 \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .
- Let  $\mathbf{A} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell \times \ell' T}$  be any fixed matrix and let  $I \subseteq [\rho]$  be any fixed set of indices. For each  $i \in I$ , let  $S_i \leftarrow \{j + \ell \cdot (i-1) \mid j \in \hat{S}_i\}$  be the shifted set of indices, and define

$$J = \{j \in S_i \text{ for some } i \in I \mid j \in [\ell']\} \subseteq [\ell'].$$

Write  $\mathbf{A} = [\mathbf{A}_1 \mid \cdots \mid \mathbf{A}_{\ell'}]$ , where each  $\mathbf{A}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell \times T}$ . Let  $\hat{\mathbf{A}} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell \times \lambda |I|T}$  be the submatrix of  $\mathbf{A}$  formed by taking only the blocks of  $\mathbf{A}$  indexed by the set J (namely, the blocks  $\mathbf{A}_j$  for  $j \in J$ ). Next, for  $i \in [\rho]$ , define  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell}$  as follows:

$$\alpha_j^{(i)} = \begin{cases} \alpha_{j+\ell \cdot (i-1)} & \text{if } j \in \hat{S}_i \\ 0 & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

By construction,  $\alpha^{(i)}$  contains exactly  $\lambda$  non-zero entries (as specified by the set  $\hat{S}_i$ ). Then, for any  $i \in [\rho] \setminus I$ ,

$$\Pr[\boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} \in \operatorname{span}(\hat{\mathbf{A}})] = \Pr[\exists \mathbf{v} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\lambda|I|T} : \boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} = \hat{\mathbf{A}}\mathbf{v}] = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* As in the proof of Claim C.11, it suffices to check that these properties hold for truly random  $(\hat{S}_1, \ldots, \hat{S}_{\rho}, \boldsymbol{\alpha}) \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{T}_{\lambda,\ell}^{\rho} \times \mathbb{Z}_2^{\rho\ell}$ . We show each property below:

- Since  $\alpha \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2^{\rho\ell}$ , for all  $j \in [\rho\ell]$ ,  $\Pr[\alpha_j = 0] = 1/2$ . Since  $|\hat{S}_i| = \lambda$ , we have that  $\Pr[\forall j \in \hat{S}_i : \alpha_j = 0] = 1/2^{\lambda} = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , and the claim holds.
- Let  $\hat{\mathbf{A}}$  be the matrix defined above and let  $\hat{\mathbf{a}}_j^\mathsf{T} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\lambda|I|T}$  denote the  $j^{\text{th}}$  row of  $\hat{\mathbf{A}}$ . Let  $n = \text{rank}(\hat{\mathbf{A}}) \leq \lambda |I|T \leq \lambda \rho T = \ell/(36\lambda)$ . This means that there exists a collection of indices  $j_1, \ldots, j_n \in [\ell]$  such that the collection  $\{\hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_1}^\mathsf{T}, \ldots, \hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_n}^\mathsf{T}\}$  is linearly independent and  $\text{span}(\hat{\mathbf{A}}^\mathsf{T}) = \text{span}(\{\hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_1}^\mathsf{T}, \ldots, \hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_n}^\mathsf{T}\})$ . By construction  $\hat{\mathbf{A}}$  only depends on  $\mathbf{A}$  and the sets  $\hat{S}_i$  where  $i \in I$ . This means that we can sample the sets  $\hat{S}_i$  where  $i \notin I$  after fixing  $\hat{\mathbf{A}}$  and the set of indices  $\{j_1, \ldots, j_n\}$ . In this case, we will show that if we sample  $\hat{S}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{T}_{\lambda,\ell}$ , then with negligible probability,  $|\hat{S}_i \cap \{j_1, \ldots, j_n\}| \geq \lambda/2$ . Let  $K = |\hat{S}_i \cap \{j_1, \ldots, j_n\}|$ . In the proof of Claim C.11, it was sufficient to show that  $K < \lambda$  with overwhelming probability because we were working over a super-polynomial-size field. Here, we require a stronger property that  $K < \lambda/2$  with overwhelming probability because we are working over the binary field. Take any  $\lambda \geq k \geq \lambda/2$ .

$$\Pr[K = k] = \frac{\binom{n}{k} \binom{\ell - n}{\lambda - k}}{\binom{\ell}{\lambda}} \le \left(\frac{en}{k}\right)^k (e\ell)^{\lambda - k} \left(\frac{\lambda}{\ell}\right)^{\lambda},$$

where we have used the fact that  $\left(\frac{n}{k}\right)^k \leq {n \choose k} \leq \left(\frac{en}{k}\right)^k$ . Since  $n \leq \ell/(36\lambda)$  and  $\lambda \geq k \geq \lambda/2$ , we have that

$$\Pr[K=k] \leq \frac{(e\lambda)^{\lambda}}{\ell^k} \left(\frac{n}{k}\right)^k \leq \frac{(e\lambda)^{\lambda}}{\ell^k} \left(\frac{2\ell}{36\lambda^2}\right)^k = \frac{(e\lambda)^{\lambda}2^k}{(36\lambda^2)^k} \leq \frac{(2e)^{\lambda}}{36^{\lambda/2}} = \frac{(2e)^{\lambda}}{6^{\lambda}} = \operatorname{negl}(\lambda).$$

Then, by a union bound  $\Pr[\lambda \geq K \geq \lambda/2] = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Thus, with overwhelming probability,  $K = |\hat{S}_i \cap \{j_1, \dots, j_n\}| < \lambda/2$ . This means that there exist at least  $\lambda/2$  indices  $j_k^* \in \hat{S}_i$  where  $j_k^* \notin \{j_1, \dots, j_n\}$ . Now as in the proof of Claim C.11, since  $\hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_k^*} \in \operatorname{span}(\hat{\mathbf{A}}^\mathsf{T})$ , there exists scalars  $\beta_1, \dots, \beta_n \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  such that  $\hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_k^*}^\mathsf{T} = \sum_{\gamma \in [n]} \beta_\gamma \hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_\gamma}^\mathsf{T}$ . This means that if there exists  $\mathbf{v} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\lambda|I|T}$  such that  $\mathbf{\alpha}^{(i)} = \hat{\mathbf{A}}\mathbf{v}$ , then

<span id="page-65-0"></span>
$$\alpha_{j_k^*}^{(i)} = \hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_k^*}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v} = \sum_{\gamma \in [n]} \beta_{\gamma} \hat{\mathbf{a}}_{j_{\gamma}}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v} = \sum_{\gamma \in [n]} \beta_{\gamma} \alpha_{j_{\gamma}}^{(i)}. \tag{D.5}$$

Since  $j_k^* \in \hat{S}_i$ , by construction,  $\alpha_{j_k^*}^{(i)} = \alpha_{j_k^* + \ell \cdot (i-1)}$ , which is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_2$  and independent of  $\beta_{\gamma}$  and  $\alpha_{j_{\gamma}}^{(i)}$  for all  $\gamma \in [n]$ . Thus, over the randomness of  $\alpha$ , Eq. (D.5) holds with probability 1/2 for each index  $j_k^*$ . Thus, for any  $i \in [\rho] \setminus I$ , with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $\hat{S}_i$ , there are at least  $\lambda/2$  such indices  $j_k^* \in \hat{S}_i$ , and since each  $\alpha_{j_k^*}^{(i)}$  is sampled independently and uniformly over  $\mathbb{Z}_2$ , we have that

$$\Pr[\exists \mathbf{v} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\lambda|I|T} : \boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} = \hat{\mathbf{A}}\mathbf{v}] \leq \frac{1}{2^{\lambda/2}} = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

**Lemma D.10.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_1(A)$ .

*Proof.* Since  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$  samples  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$  using the same procedure as  $\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$ , the output distributions of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$  are identical.

**Lemma D.11.** For all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_2(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* Follows by the same argument as the proof of Lemma D.5.

**Lemma D.12.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_3(A)$ .

*Proof.* Follows by the Chinese remainder theorem (as in the proof of Lemma D.6).  $\Box$ 

**Lemma D.13.** If G is a secure PRG, then for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_4(\mathcal{A})$ .

Proof. In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ , the challenger samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell'}$  while in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , the challenger samples  $\hat{y}_j' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}_j' = \hat{\omega}_i$  where  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$  for  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in [\rho]$ . For the indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ ,  $\hat{y}_j' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$ . These distributions are identical as long as there exists some  $j \in S_i$  where  $\alpha_j \neq 0$  for each  $i \in [\rho]$ . Since G is a secure PRG, this follows by Claim D.9.

**Lemma D.14.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_5(A)$ .

*Proof.* First,  $\mathbf{y}'$  is sampled identically in the two distributions. It suffices to show that once we fix the PRG seed  $\mathbf{s}$  and the vector  $\mathbf{y}' \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$ , there is a one-to-one correspondence between the value of  $\hat{\omega}_i$  and the value of  $r_i$ . In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ ,  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(\bar{t}_i', \bar{t}_i'h)$  where

$$\bar{t}_i' = \prod_{j \in S_i} \bar{t}_j^{\alpha_j} = \prod_{j \in S_i} (g^{s_j \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{e}_j})^{\alpha_j}.$$

Since g generates a subgroup of order p'q', and  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$ , we have that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ ,  $g^{\alpha_j s_j \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} = g^{\alpha_j s_j (\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}}$ . Similarly, since h has order 2,  $h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{e}_j} = h^{y_j} = h^{\hat{y}_j'}$ . This means that

$$\bar{t}_i' = \prod_{j \in S_i} (g^{s_j \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{v} h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{e}_j)^{\alpha_j} = \prod_{j \in S_i} g^{\alpha_j s_j (\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{v} h^{\alpha_j \hat{y}_j'} = g^{\omega_i (\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{v} h^{\hat{\omega}_i},$$

where  $\omega_i = \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j$  and  $\hat{\omega}_i = \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}_j'$ . Since  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(\bar{t}_i', \bar{t}_i'h)$ , we conclude that once we fix the seed s (which together with the CRS determines the value of  $\omega_i$ ) and the vector  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}'$ , then the value of  $r_i$  is entirely dependent on the value of  $\hat{\omega}_i$  (mod 2). By the same argument as in the proof of Lemma D.7, there is a one-to-one correspondence between the value of  $\hat{\omega}_i$  and  $r_i$ , and both distributions enforce this correspondence. As such, these two distributions are identical.

**Lemma D.15.** If G is a secure PRG, then for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_6(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* The challenger samples  $\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}$  identically in the two experiments, so  $N, g, h, \mathbf{v}, s_1, \ldots, s_{\ell'}$  are identically distributed in the two experiments. so it suffices to consider its responses to the challenge queries. In both experiments, on each query, the challenger starts by sending the adversary a random string  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ , and the adversary replies with a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ . The challenger then replies with a commitment  $\sigma = (\mathbf{s}, \overline{c})$  and a set of proofs  $\{\pi_i\}_{i \in I}$ , where  $\pi_i = \{(j, \overline{t}_j, u_j)\}_{j \in S_i}$ . We show that the challenger's responses are statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments. To this end, we define the following variables:

• For  $i \in [\rho]$ , let  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell}$  be the vector where  $\hat{y}_j^{(i)} = \hat{y}_{j+\ell\cdot(i-1)}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . In other words,  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^{\mathsf{T}} = [(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(1)})^{\mathsf{T}} \mid \cdots \mid (\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(\rho)})^{\mathsf{T}}] \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell'}$ .

• For  $i \in [\rho]$ , define  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} = (\alpha_1^{(i)}, \dots, \alpha_\ell^{(i)})^\top \in \mathbb{Z}_N^\ell$  as follows:

$$\alpha_j^{(i)} = \begin{cases} \alpha_{j+\ell \cdot (i-1)} & \text{if } j \in \hat{S}_i \\ 0 & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

We now consider the different components in the two experiments:

- The string r is independently and uniformly sampled from  $\{0,1\}^{\rho}$  in both experiments.
- The seed s is independently and uniformly sampled from  $\{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  in both experiments, so the seed s, the sets  $S_1, \ldots, S_{\rho}$ , and the vector  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}$  are identically distributed as well.
- The vector  $\mathbf{y}'$  is sampled uniformly from  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$  in both experiments. Since g generates a group of order p'q', the commitment  $\overline{c} = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}} = g^{(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$  is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ .
- For all  $i \in I$ , both experiments set  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$  and sample  $\hat{\omega}_i \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_2$  subject to  $r_i = \mathsf{LEQ}(g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{\omega}_i}, g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{\omega}_i+1})$ . This means that the vectors  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  for  $i \in I$  are identically distributed in the two experiments. Then, for  $j \in S_i$ , we have that  $\bar{t}_j = g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}'_j}$ , so the components  $\bar{t}_j$  for  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$  are identically distributed.

It suffices to show that the remaining components  $\{u_j\}_{j\in S_i}$  for  $i\in I$  are drawn from statistically indistinguishable distributions (from the view of the adversary). Since  $u_j = H(\overline{u}_{1,j}, \ldots, \overline{u}_{T,j})$ , it suffices to show that the elements  $\{\overline{u}_{\tau,j}\}_{\tau\in[T],j\in S_i}$  are statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments. First, let

$$J = \{j \in S_i \text{ for some } i \in I \mid j \in [\ell']\}$$

be the set of indices that appear in some set  $S_i$  for  $i \in I$ . Next, let  $\overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,j} = g^{\mathbf{z}_{\tau,j}} h^{\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,j}}$  be the subgroup decomposition of the public-key components. Then, in both experiments, the challenger computes  $\overline{u}_{\tau,j}$  as

$$\overline{u}_{\tau,j} = \prod_{k \in [\ell']} \overline{z}_{\tau,j,k}^{y_k} = g^{(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{z}_{\tau,j} h^{(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}} \hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,j}.$$

Since  $\mathbf{y}'$  is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ , it suffices to consider the distribution of  $\overline{u}_{\tau,j}$  in the  $\mathbb{H}$  subgroup, or equivalently, the distribution of  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\tau,j}$  over  $\mathbb{Z}_2$ . Let  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell' \times T}$  be the matrix whose columns are  $\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{1,i},\ldots,\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{T,i}$ , and let  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell' \times \ell' T}$  be the matrix

$$\hat{\mathbf{Z}} = [\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_1 \mid \cdots \mid \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{\ell'}].$$

Let  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell' \times \lambda |I|T}$  be the submatrix of  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$  formed by taking only the blocks of  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$  indexed by the set J (namely, the blocks  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_j$  for  $j \in J$ ). In particular, the values of  $h^{(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' \in \mathbb{H}^{\lambda|I|T}$  precisely coincide with the components in the  $\mathbb{H}$ -subgroup of  $\overline{u}_{\tau,j}$  for all  $\tau \in [T]$ ,  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$ . Thus, it suffices to show that the distributions of  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\lambda|I|T}$  are statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments. First, for  $i \in [\rho]$ , let  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)} \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\ell \times \lambda|I|T}$  be matrices such that

$$\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' = \left[ \begin{array}{c} \hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(1)} \ \vdots \ \hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(\rho)} \end{array} \right],$$

This means that

<span id="page-68-1"></span>
$$(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^{\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' = \sum_{i \in [\rho]} \left( (\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^{\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)} \right) \in \mathbb{Z}_2^{\lambda|I|T}.$$
(D.6)

By definition,  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$  is a *fixed* matrix (determined by the CRS and the adversary's public key) and independent of  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}'$ . Since each  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is sampled independently, we can consider each term individually in this summation:

- If  $i \in I$ , then as argued above,  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ , and correspondingly, so is the product  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)}$ .
- If  $i \notin I$ , then the  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  in the two experiments are sampled from distinct distributions. In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_2^\ell$  subject to  $\hat{\omega}_i = \sum_{j \in [\ell]} \alpha_j^{(i)} \hat{y}_j^{(i)}$ , while in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_2^\ell$ .

Since  $i \notin I$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$  is a fixed matrix, we can appeal to Claim D.9 (for the  $i^{\text{th}}$  block of  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$ ) and conclude that with overwhelming probability,  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} \notin \text{span}(\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)})$ . By Claim C.12, this means that the distribution of  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^{\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)}$  in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  (where  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is uniform subject to a linear constraint  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} \notin \text{span}(\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)})$ ) is statistically indistinguishable from its distribution in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$  (where  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is uniform).

Since every term in Eq. (D.6) is either statistically indistinguishable or identically distributed in the two experiments, we conclude that  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^T \hat{\mathbf{Z}}'$  is also statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments. Correspondingly, this means that the components  $\overline{u}_{\tau,j}$  for  $\tau \in [T]$ ,  $j \in S_i$ , and  $i \in I$  are also statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments.

Since each consecutive pair of hybrid experiments is statistically indistinguishable (or identically distributed), the theorem follows.  $\Box$ 

### <span id="page-68-0"></span>E Dual-Mode Hidden-Bits Generators from DCR

In this section, we show how to construct dual-mode hidden-bits generators from the DCR assumption. As in Section 5, we begin with a basic construction (Construction E.2) and then show how to extend it to obtain one with security against malicious verifiers (Construction E.16). Both constructions are structurally similar to the corresponding constructions from QR (Constructions 5.3 and 5.9, respectively). One difference between the two construction is that we now use a universal hash function to extract the hidden bit rather than the LEQ predicate. In addition, we rely on a slightly different verification check. This is because in the QR constructions, the public key, commitment, and proofs are all elements in  $\mathbb{J}_N$  and membership in  $\mathbb{J}_N$  is efficiently-decidable. The analog of  $\mathbb{J}_N$  in the DCR setting is the subgroup of quadratic residues in  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$ , which is not an efficiently-decidable language. Thus, a malicious prover or verifier could publish public-keys, commitments, or proofs that are quadratic non-residues over  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$  to try and break soundness or zero-knowledge. We handle this case by adjusting the verification relation.

#### E.1 Dual-Mode Hidden-Bits Generator from DCR

In this section, we construct a standard dual-mode hidden-bits generator from the DCR assumption (without malicious security). This is an analog of Construction 5.3 from the QR assumption. Our

construction is inspired by the trapdoor hash function of [DGI<sup>+</sup>19, Appendix A]. We begin by recalling some basic notation as well as the DCR assumption.

**Notation.** Let N=pq be a product of safe primes p,q. Our construction works over the group  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$ , which splits into two subgroups  $\mathbb{H}:=\{(1+N)^i\mid i\in[N]\}$  and  $\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_N:=\{x^N\mid x\in\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*\}$  of coprime orders N and  $\varphi(N)$ , respectively. In our analysis, we will use the fact that if  $x\in\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*=\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_N\times\mathbb{H}$ , then  $x^2\in\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_{2N}\times\mathbb{H}$ . When N is a product of safe primes  $p=2p'+1,\ q=2q'+1$ , the subgroup  $\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_{2N}$  of  $2N^{th}$  residues is cyclic (and has order p'q'). In the following, we write g to denote a generator of  $\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_{2N}$  and h=(1+N) to denote a generator of  $\mathbb{H}$ . We will typically denote elements of  $\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_{2N}\times\mathbb{H}$  with a bar (e.g.,  $\bar{c},\bar{t}$ ). In the analysis, we often analyze elements of  $\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_{2N}\times\mathbb{H}$  by examining their components in their respective subgroups: we write  $\bar{c}=g^ch^{\hat{c}}\in\mathbb{N}\mathbb{R}_{2N}\times\mathbb{H}$  where  $c\in\mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  and  $\hat{c}\in\mathbb{Z}_N$ .

**Definition E.1** (Decisional Composite Residuosity Assumption [Pai99]). A safe prime modulus sampler SampleModulus satisfies the decisional composite residuosity (DCR) assumption if for all efficient adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , and sampling  $(N, p, q) \leftarrow \mathsf{SampleModulus}(1^{\lambda}), x \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$ ,

$$\left|\Pr[\mathcal{A}(N,x)=1] - \Pr[\mathcal{A}(N,x^N)]\right| = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

<span id="page-69-0"></span>Construction E.2 (Dual-Mode Hidden-Bits Generator from DCR). Our DCR-based dual-mode hidden-bits generator (HBG) goes as follows:

- Setup( $1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}$ , mode)  $\rightarrow$  (crs, sk): Sample  $(N, p, q) \leftarrow$  SampleModulus( $1^{\lambda}$ ). Let g be a generator of  $\mathbb{NR}_{2N}$  and h = 1 + N be the generator of  $\mathbb{H}$ . The setup algorithm samples a vector  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ , scalars  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\rho} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$  and sets  $\hat{\mathbf{w}}_i \in \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_N$  for  $i \in [\rho]$  as follows:
  - If mode = hiding, set  $\hat{\mathbf{w}}_i \leftarrow \mathbf{e}_i$ , where  $\mathbf{e}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\rho}$  is the  $i^{\text{th}}$  basis vector.
  - If mode = binding, set  $\hat{\mathbf{w}}_i \leftarrow \mathbf{0}$ .

Finally, it sample a hash function  $H \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{H}$  where  $\mathcal{H}$  is a family of hash functions with domain  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}$  and range  $\{0,1\}$ . Output  $\mathsf{crs} = (N,g,h,H,g^{\mathbf{v}},g^{s_1\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}_1},\ldots,g^{s_\rho\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}_\rho})$ .

- KeyGen(crs)  $\rightarrow$  (pk,sk): On input crs =  $(N,g,h,H,\overline{\mathbf{v}},\overline{\mathbf{w}}_1,\ldots,\overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\rho})$ , sample  $a,b_1,\ldots,b_{\rho} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ . Output pk =  $(\overline{\mathbf{v}}^{b_1}\overline{\mathbf{w}}_1^a,\ldots,\overline{\mathbf{v}}^{b_{\rho}}\overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\rho}^a)$  and sk =  $(a,b_1,\ldots,b_{\rho})$ .
- GenBits(crs, pk)  $\to$   $(\sigma, r, \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [\rho]})$ : On input crs  $= (N, g, h, H, \overline{\mathbf{v}}, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\rho})$  and pk  $= (\overline{\mathbf{z}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\rho})$ , sample  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{|N^2/4|}$  and compute for all  $i \in [\rho]$ :

$$\overline{c} \leftarrow \prod_{j \in [\rho]} \overline{v}_j^{y_j} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{t}_i \leftarrow \prod_{j \in [\rho]} \overline{w}_{i,j}^{y_j} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{u}_i \leftarrow \prod_{j \in [\rho]} (\overline{z}_{i,j}^2)^{y_j}.$$

For each  $i \in [\rho]$ , let  $r_i \leftarrow H(\overline{t}_i^2) \in \{0,1\}$ . Output  $\sigma = \overline{c}$ , r, and  $\pi = \{(\overline{t}_i, \overline{u}_i)\}_{i \in [\rho]}$ .

• Verify(crs, sk,  $\sigma$ , i,  $r_i$ ,  $\pi_i$ ): On input crs =  $(N, g, h, H, \overline{\mathbf{v}}, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\rho})$ , sk =  $(a, b_1, \dots, b_{\rho})$ ,  $\sigma = \overline{c}$ ,  $i \in [\rho]$ ,  $r_i \in \{0, 1\}$ , and  $\pi_i = (\overline{t}_i, \overline{u}_i)$ , output 1 if  $\overline{u}_i = (\overline{t}_i^a \overline{c}^{b_i})^2$  and  $r_i = H(\overline{t}_i^2)$ . Otherwise, output 0.

Correctness and security analysis. We now state the correctness and security theorems for Construction E.2 and give the proofs in Appendix E.1.1.

<span id="page-70-1"></span>**Theorem E.3** (Correctness). Construction E.2 is correct.

<span id="page-70-3"></span>**Theorem E.4** (Succinctness). Construction E.2 is succinct.

<span id="page-70-4"></span>**Theorem E.5** (CRS Indistinguishability). Suppose the DCR assumption holds with respect to SampleModulus. Then, Construction E.2 satisfies CRS indistinguishability.

<span id="page-70-5"></span>**Theorem E.6** (Statistical Binding in Binding Mode). Construction E.2 satisfies statistical binding in binding mode.

<span id="page-70-2"></span>**Theorem E.7** (Statistical Simulation in Hiding Mode). If  $\mathcal{H}$  is a universal hash, then Construction E.2 satisfies statistical simulation in hiding mode.

### <span id="page-70-0"></span>E.1.1 Analysis of Construction E.2 (Dual-Mode HBG from DCR)

In this section, we give the proofs for the correctness and security theorems (Theorems E.3 to E.7) for the dual-mode hidden-bits generator from the DCR assumption (Construction E.2).

**Proof of Theorem E.3 (Correctness).** Fix  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , a polynomial  $\rho = \rho(\lambda)$ , an index  $i \in [\rho]$ , and a mode mode  $\in \{\text{binding}\}$ . Let  $\operatorname{crs} \leftarrow \operatorname{Setup}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}, \operatorname{mode})$ ,  $(\operatorname{pk}, \operatorname{sk}) \leftarrow \operatorname{KeyGen}(\operatorname{crs})$ , and  $(\sigma, r, \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [\rho]}) \leftarrow \operatorname{GenBits}(\operatorname{crs}, \operatorname{pk})$ . By construction,  $\operatorname{crs} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}_1}, \dots, g^{s_{\rho}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}_{\rho}})$  for some  $\mathbf{v} \in \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{|N^2/4|}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{w}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{w}}_{\rho} \in \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_N$ . Then,  $\operatorname{sk} = (a, b_1, \dots, b_{\rho})$  and

$$\mathsf{pk} = \left(g^{b_1\mathbf{v} + as_1\mathbf{v}}h^{a\hat{\mathbf{w}}_1}, \dots, g^{b_\rho\mathbf{v} + as_\rho\mathbf{v}}h^{a\hat{\mathbf{w}}_\rho}\right) = \left(g^{(as_1 + b_1)\mathbf{v}}h^{a\hat{\mathbf{w}}_1}, \dots, g^{(as_\rho + b_\rho)\mathbf{v}}h^{a\hat{\mathbf{w}}_\rho}.\right)$$

Similarly, we have  $\sigma = \overline{c} = \prod_{j \in [\rho]} g^{v_j y_j} = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}}, \ r_i = H(\overline{t}_i^2) \text{ and } \pi_i = (\overline{t}_i, \overline{u}_i) \text{ where } \mathbf{v} = \mathbf{v}$ 

$$\bar{t}_i = \prod_{j \in [\rho]} \left( g^{\mathbf{s}_i v_j} h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}_{i,j}} \right)^{y_j} = g^{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \hat{\mathbf{w}}_i} 
\bar{u}_i = \prod_{j \in [\rho]} \left( g^{(as_i + b_i)v_j} h^{a\hat{\mathbf{w}}_{i,j}} \right)^{2y_j} = (g^{(as_i + b_i)\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} h^{a\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \hat{\mathbf{w}}_i})^2.$$

Consider now the behavior of Verify(crs, sk,  $\sigma$ , i,  $r_i$ ,  $\pi_i$ ). By construction,  $r_i = H(\bar{t}_i^2)$ , so it suffices to check that  $\bar{u}_i = (\bar{t}_i^a \bar{c}^{b_i})^2$ . From the above relations,

$$(\overline{t}_i^a \overline{c}^{b_i})^2 = \left(g^{s_i \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \hat{\mathbf{w}}_i}\right)^{2a} \left(g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}}\right)^{2b_i} = \left(g^{(as_i + b_i) \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} h^{a \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \hat{\mathbf{w}}_i}\right)^2 = \overline{u}_i,$$

and the verification algorithm outputs 1.

**Proof of Theorem E.4 (Succinctness).** The size of the commitment in Construction E.2 is a single element in  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}$ , which has length  $2 \lceil \log N \rceil = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ .

**Proof of Theorem E.5 (CRS Indistinguishability).** First, under the DCR assumption, for  $N \leftarrow \mathsf{SampleModulus}(1^{\lambda})$ , the following two distributions are computationally indistinguishable:

$$\{x \overset{\mathrm{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^* : (N,x)\} \overset{c}{\approx} \{x \overset{\mathrm{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^* : (N,x^N)\}.$$

This means that the following two distributions are also computationally indistinguishable:

$$\{x \overset{\mathrm{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^* : (N, x^2)\} \overset{c}{\approx} \{x \overset{\mathrm{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^* : (N, x^{2N})\}.$$

This means that the uniform distribution over  $\mathbb{NR}_{2N} \times \mathbb{H}$  is computationally indistinguishable from the uniform distribution over  $\mathbb{NR}_{2N}$ . We can now appeal to the following theorem from [BG10]:

<span id="page-71-0"></span>Claim E.8 ([BG10, §B.2]). Suppose a safe prime product modulus sampler SampleModulus satisfies the DCR assumption. Then, for all polynomials  $\rho = \rho(\lambda)$ , all fixed vectors  $\hat{\mathbf{w}} \in \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ , and all efficient adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , if we sample  $(N,p,q) \leftarrow \mathsf{SampleModulus}(1^{\lambda})$ ,  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$ ,  $s \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$ , where p = 2p' + 1 and q = 2q' + 1, we have that

$$\left|\Pr[\mathcal{A}(N,g,g^{\mathbf{v}},g^{s\mathbf{v}})=1] - \Pr[\mathcal{A}(N,g,g^{\mathbf{v}},g^{s\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}})=1]\right| = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda),$$

where g is a generator of  $\mathbb{NR}_{2N}$  and h = (1+N) is a generator of  $\mathbb{H}$ .

First, Claim E.8 holds even if  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$  and  $s \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$  since the statistical distance between  $\{r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor} : r \bmod p'q'\}$  and  $\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{p'q'})$  is negligible. The theorem now follows by an analogous hybrid argument as in the proof of Theorem 5.6.

**Proof of Theorem E.6 (Statistical Binding).** Recall that in binding mode, the common reference string is given by

$$\operatorname{crs} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{w}}, \dots, g^{s_{\rho} \mathbf{w}}).$$

We define the (inefficient) Open algorithm as follows:

• Open(crs,  $\sigma$ )  $\to r$ : On input a crs =  $(N, g, h, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}}, \dots, g^{s_{\rho} \mathbf{v}})$  and a commitment  $\sigma = \overline{c} \in \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$  (outputting  $\bot$  if the components do not have this form), the open algorithm recovers  $s_1, \dots, s_{\rho}$ . It computes  $r_i \leftarrow H((\overline{c}^{s_i})^2)$  for each  $i \in [\rho]$  and outputs r.

To complete the proof, we use a hybrid argument:

• Hyb<sub>0</sub>: This is the real soundness experiment. The challenger samples  $\operatorname{crs} \leftarrow \operatorname{\mathsf{Setup}}(1^\lambda, 1^\rho, \operatorname{\mathsf{binding}})$  and  $(\operatorname{\mathsf{pk}}, \operatorname{\mathsf{sk}}) \leftarrow \operatorname{\mathsf{KeyGen}}(\operatorname{\mathsf{crs}})$  and gives  $(\operatorname{\mathsf{crs}}, \operatorname{\mathsf{pk}})$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ . Here,

$$\mathsf{crs} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}}, \dots, g^{s_\rho \mathbf{v}}) \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{pk} = (g^{(as_1 + b_1)\mathbf{v}}, \dots, g^{(as_\rho + b_\rho)\mathbf{v}}).$$

The adversary can make queries to the verification oracle, and on each query  $(\sigma, i, r_i, \pi_i)$ , the challenger replies with  $\mathsf{Verify}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{sk}, \sigma, i, r_i, \pi_i)$ . At the end of the game, the adversary outputs a tuple  $(\sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*)$  and the output of the experiment is 1 if  $r^* \neq r_i$  where  $r \leftarrow \mathsf{Open}(\mathsf{crs}, \sigma^*)$  and  $\mathsf{Verify}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{sk}, \sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*) = 1$ .

•  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$ : Same as  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$  except the challenger samples the scalars  $s_1, \ldots, s_\rho$  and the secret key components  $a, b_1, \ldots, b_\rho$  uniformly at random from  $\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}$  (instead of  $\mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ ).

- Hyb<sub>2</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>1</sub> except the challenger computes Verify(crs, sk,  $\sigma$ , i,  $r_i$ ,  $\pi_i$ ) using the following modified procedure. Let  $\sigma = \overline{c} \in \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$ , and write  $\overline{c}^2 = g^c h^{\hat{c}}$  for some  $c \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  and  $\hat{c} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . Similarly, parse  $\pi_i = (\overline{t}_i, \overline{u}_i) \in (\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*)^2$  and write  $\overline{t}_i^2$  as  $g^{t_i} h^{\hat{t}_i}$  for  $t_i \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  and  $\hat{t}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . Next, the challenger outputs 0 if  $\overline{u}_i \notin \mathbb{NR}_{2N} \times \mathbb{H}$ . Otherwise, it writes  $\overline{u}_i$  as  $g^{u_i} h^{\hat{u}_i}$  for  $u_i \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  and  $\hat{u}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . Then the challenger does the following:
  - If  $r_i \neq H(\overline{t}_i^2)$ , output 0.
  - If  $\hat{c} \neq 0$  or  $\hat{t}_i \neq 0$ , then output 0.
  - If  $t_i \neq s_i c$ , then output 0.
  - Otherwise, take any  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$  such that  $\mathbf{y}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v} = c$ . Output 1 if  $u_i = (as_i + b_i)\mathbf{y}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}$  and  $\hat{u}_i = 0$ . Otherwise (or if no such  $\mathbf{y}$  exists), output 0.

Importantly, the challenger's responses to the verification queries in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$  depend only on the public components (i.e.,  $\mathsf{crs}$  and  $\mathsf{pk}$ ).

For an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ , we write  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i(\mathcal{A})$  to denote the output distribution of an execution of experiment  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i$  with adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ . We now show that the output distribution of each adjacent pair of hybrid experiments is statistically indistinguishable.

**Lemma E.9.** For all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_1(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* The statistical distance between  $\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{|N^2/4|})$  and  $\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'})$  satisfies

<span id="page-72-0"></span>
$$\Delta(\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4\rfloor}),\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'})) = 1 - \frac{Np'q'}{\lfloor N^2/4\rfloor} = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda), \tag{E.1}$$

since  $1/p', 1/q' = \text{negl}(\lambda)$ . Since  $\rho = \text{poly}(\lambda)$ , the claim follows by a union bound.

**Lemma E.10.** For all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_2(\mathcal{A})$ .

Proof. In Hyb<sub>1</sub> and Hyb<sub>2</sub>, the challenger evaluates Verify at most Q+1 times where  $Q=\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  is the bound on the number of queries the adversary makes. For  $j\in\{0,\ldots,Q+1\}$ , let  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j}$  denote the experiment where the first j queries are handling according to the specification in  $\operatorname{Hyb}_2$  while the remaining queries are handling according to the specification in  $\operatorname{Hyb}_1$ . By construction,  $\operatorname{Hyb}_1 \equiv \operatorname{Hyb}_{1,0}$  and  $\operatorname{Hyb}_2 \equiv \operatorname{Hyb}_{1,Q+1}$ . Consider  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  and  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j}$  for  $j\in[Q+1]$ . These two experiments only differ in how the challenger computes the output for the  $j^{\text{th}}$  Verify call. Moreover, by construction of  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  and  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j}$ , all of the adversary's queries prior to the  $j^{\text{th}}$  query are handled according to the specification in  $\operatorname{Hyb}_2$ , which depend only on the public components crs and pk. Let  $(\sigma,i,r_i,\pi_i)$  be the arguments to the  $j^{\text{th}}$  Verify call. As in the specification of  $\operatorname{Hyb}_2$ , parse  $\sigma=\bar{c}\in\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$  and  $\pi_i=(\bar{t}_i,\bar{u}_i)\in\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$ . First, if  $\bar{u}_i$  is not a quadratic residue (i.e.,  $\bar{u}_i\notin\mathbb{NR}_{2N}\times\mathbb{H}$ ), then the challenger in  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j}$  always outputs 0. We argue that this is the case in  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  as well. By construction of Verify, the output is 1 only if  $\bar{u}_i=(\bar{t}_i^a\bar{c}^{b_i})^2$ . But if  $\bar{u}_i$  is not a quadratic residue, this relation is never satisfied, and so the output in  $\operatorname{Hyb}_{1,j}$  is also 0. Thus, it suffices to only consider the case where  $\bar{u}_i$  is a quadratic residue. Then, define  $c,t_i,u_i\in\mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  and  $\hat{c},\hat{t}_i,\hat{u}_i\in\mathbb{Z}_N$  such that  $\bar{c}^2=g^ch^c, \bar{t}_i^2=g^{t_i}h^{\hat{t}_i}$ , and  $\bar{u}_i=g^{u_i}h^{\hat{u}_i}$ . We consider the different cases:

• Suppose  $r_i \neq H(\overline{t}_i^2)$ . Then, the output in both experiments is 0.

• Suppose  $\hat{c} \neq 0$  or  $\hat{t}_i \neq 0$ . We argue that with overwhelming probability, the output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  is 0. For the output to be 1 in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$ , it must be the case that  $\overline{u}_i = (\overline{t}_i^a \overline{c}^{b_i})^2$ , or equivalently,

$$u_i = at_i + b_i c \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$$
 and  $\hat{u}_i = a\hat{t}_i + b_i \hat{c} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ .

In both  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ , the public parameters are independent of the values of  $a \mod N$  and  $b_i \mod N$ . This follows from the fact that  $a, b_i \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}$ , and the adversary only sees elements  $g^{(as_i+b_i)\mathbf{v}}$ , where g generates a group of order p'q' (and  $\gcd(p'q',N)=1$ ). Next, since a and  $b_i$  are uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}$ , the values  $a \mod N$  and  $b_i \mod N$  are distributed uniformly and independently of the rest of the public parameters. Since the responses to all of the adversary's queries prior to its  $j^{\text{th}}$  query only depend on the public parameters, the conditional distribution of  $a \mod N$  and  $b_i \mod N$  given the adversary's view up to the time of its  $j^{\text{th}}$  query is uniform and independently random. Since at least one of  $\hat{c}$  and  $\hat{t}_i$  is non-zero, this means that the value of  $a\hat{t}_i + b_i\hat{c} \mod N$  is independently and uniformly random over  $\mathbb{Z}_N$ . Therefore,  $\hat{u}_i = a\hat{t}_i + b_i\hat{c}$  with probability at most  $1/N = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . This means that the output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,i-1}$  is 0 with overwhelming probability.

• Suppose that  $t_i \neq s_i c \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$ . We only need to consider the case where  $\hat{c} = 0$  and  $\hat{t}_i = 0$ . We show that in this case, the output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  is 0 with overwhelming probability. For the output to be 1 in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$ , it must be the case that  $\overline{u}_i = (\overline{t}_i^a \overline{c}^{b_i})^2$ , or equivalently,

$$u_i = at_i + b_i c \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$$
 and  $\hat{u}_i = a\hat{t}_i + b_i \hat{c} = 0 \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ .

The only components in crs and pk that depend on a and  $b_i$  are the public-key components  $g^{(as_i+b_i)\mathbf{v}}$ . Let  $\mathbf{b} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  be the vector whose components are  $b_1, \ldots, b_{\rho}$ , and let  $\mathbf{s} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  be the vector whose components are  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\rho}$ . The public parameters  $\mathbf{pk}$  can then be expressed as a function of

$$\mathbf{Z} = [\ \mathbf{s} \ | \ \mathbf{I}_{\rho}\ ] \cdot \left[\begin{array}{c} a \\ \mathbf{b} \end{array}\right] \cdot \mathbf{v}^{\mathsf{T}} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho \times \rho},$$

where  $\mathbf{I}_{\rho} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho \times \rho}$  is the identity matrix. Namely, the components of pk consist of  $g^{\mathbf{Z}}$ . Since  $t_i \neq s_i c \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$ , by the Chinese remainder theorem, it must be the case that  $t_i \neq s_i c \pmod{p'}$  or  $t_i \neq s_i c \pmod{q'}$ . Without loss of generality, suppose that  $t_i \neq s_i c \pmod{p'}$ . In this case the vector  $[t_i \mid c \cdot \mathbf{e}_i]$  is linearly independent of the rows of the matrix  $[\mathbf{s} \pmod{p'} \mid \mathbf{I}_{\rho}]$ . Since  $a, \mathbf{b}$  are uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}$ , the components  $a \mod p'$  and  $\mathbf{b} \mod p'$  are uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'}$ . By linear independence over  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'}$ , the value of  $at_i + b_i c \pmod{p'}$  is uniformly random over  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'}$  even given  $\mathbf{Z}$ . This means that  $at_i + b_i c = u_i \pmod{p'}$  with probability at most  $1/p' = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Thus, the challenger in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  outputs 0 with overwhelming probability.

• The only remaining case is when  $\hat{c} = 0 = \hat{t}_i$ ,  $t_i = s_i c$ , and  $r_i = H(\bar{t}_i^2)$ . In this case,  $(g^{t_i})^a(g^c)^{b_i} = g^{(as_i+b_i)c}$ . Since  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ , with overwhelming probability, there will be some component that is invertible modulo p'q'. If so, there always exists  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  such that  $\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v} = c$ . Then, in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$ , the challenger outputs 1 if and only if

$$\overline{u}_i = (\overline{t}_i^a \overline{c}^{b_i})^2 = g^{at_i + b_i c} = g^{(as_i + b_i)c} = g^{(as_i + b_i)\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{v}$$

Since  $\overline{u}_i = g^{u_i} h^{\hat{u}_i}$ , this is equivalent to checking that  $u_i = (as_i + b_i)\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}$  and  $\hat{u}_i = 0$ . This is precisely the check in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j}$ .

In each case, we see that the  $j^{\text{th}}$  call to Verify is implemented correctly with overwhelming probability in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j-1}$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{1,j}$ .

To complete the proof, it suffices to show that for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , the output of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2(\mathcal{A})$  is 0 with overwhelming probability. Let  $(\sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*)$  be the adversary's output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ . The output of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$  is 1 only if  $\mathsf{Verify}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{sk}, \sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*) = 1$  and  $r_{i^*} \neq r^*$  where  $r \leftarrow \mathsf{Open}(\mathsf{crs}, \sigma^*)$ . Write  $\sigma^* = \overline{c}$ ,  $\overline{c}^2 = g^c h^{\hat{c}}$ ,  $\pi^* = (\overline{t}, \overline{u})$ ,  $\overline{t}^2 = g^t h^{\hat{t}}$ , and  $\overline{u} = g^u h^{\hat{u}}$  (if  $\overline{u}$  is not a quadratic residue in  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}$ , then the output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$  is 0). In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ , if  $\mathsf{Verify}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{sk}, \sigma^*, i^*, r^*, \pi^*) = 1$ , it must be the case that

$$r^* = H(\overline{t}^2)$$
 and  $\hat{c} = 0$  and  $\hat{t} = 0$  and  $t = s_{i^*}c$ .

Consider now the value of  $r_{i^*}$  and  $r^*$ :

- From the above,  $\bar{t}^2 = g^t h^{\hat{t}} = g^t = g^{cs_{i^*}}$ . Thus  $r^* = H(\bar{t}^2) = H(g^{cs_{i^*}})$ .
- By definition of Open,  $r_{i^*} = H((\overline{c}^{s_{i^*}})^2) = H((\overline{c}^2)^{s_{i^*}}) = H((q^c)^{s_{i^*}}) = r^*$ .

Since  $r^* = r_{i^*}$ , the output in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2(\mathcal{A})$  is 0.

**Proof of Theorem E.7 (Statistical Simulation).** We construct a simulator  $S = (S_1, S_2)$  as follows:

•  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}) \to (\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{pk}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{sk}})$ : Sample  $(N, p, q) \leftarrow \operatorname{SampleModulus}(1^{\lambda})$ , where p = 2p' + 1 and q = 2q' + 1. Let g be a generator of  $\mathbb{NR}_{2N}$  and h = 1 + N be the generator of  $\mathbb{H}$ . Sample a vector  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ , scalars  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\rho} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ , and a hash function  $H \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{H}$ . Sample  $a, b_1, \ldots, b_{\rho} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ , and set

$$\begin{split} \widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} &= \left(N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_\rho \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_\rho}\right) \\ \widetilde{\mathsf{pk}} &= \left(g^{(as_1 + b_1) \mathbf{v}} h^{a\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{(as_\rho + b_\rho) \mathbf{v}} h^{a\mathbf{e}_\rho}\right) \\ \widetilde{\mathsf{sk}} &= \left(a, b_1, \dots, b_\rho\right). \end{split}$$

Output  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathsf{sk}}$  and  $\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}, p', q', s_1, \dots, s_o)$ .

•  $S_2(\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, I, r_I) \to (\widetilde{\sigma}, \{\widetilde{\pi}_i\}_{i \in I})$ : On input  $\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{pk}}, p', q', s_1, \dots, s_{\rho})$  where

$$\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_{\rho} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\rho}})$$
 and  $\widetilde{\mathsf{pk}} = (g^{\mathbf{z}_1} h^{\hat{\mathbf{z}}_1}, \dots, g^{\mathbf{z}_{\rho}} h^{\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\rho}}),$ 

where  $\mathbf{z}_i = (as_i + b_i)\mathbf{v}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{z}}_i = a\mathbf{e}_i$  for all  $i \in [\rho]$ , a set of indices  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , and a bitstring  $r_I \in \{0,1\}^{|I|}$ , the simulator samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_{p'q'}$ . Then, it samples a vector  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}^{\rho}_N$  component-by-component: specifically, for each  $i \in [\rho]$ , it does the following:

- If  $i \notin I$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ .
- If  $i \in I$ , sample  $\hat{y}_i' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  conditioned on  $r_i = H((g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h\hat{y}_i')^2)$ . Specifically, repeatedly sample  $\hat{y}_i' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  until finding one that satisfies the relation. If no candidate is found after  $\lambda$  attempts, then abort and output  $\bot$ .

Define  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{N}$ . The simulator then sets  $\bar{t}_i = g^{s_i\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{e}_i}$  and  $\bar{u}_i = (g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{z}_i}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_i})^2$ . Output  $\tilde{\sigma} = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$  and  $\{\tilde{\pi}_i\}_{i\in I}$  where  $\tilde{\pi}_i = (\bar{t}_i, \bar{u}_i)$ .

To show that  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 0]$  and  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 1]$  are statistically indistinguishable, we use a hybrid argument:

• Hyb<sub>0</sub>: This is the experiment ExptHide[ $\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 0$ ]. Namely, the challenger begins by sampling crs  $\leftarrow$  Setup( $1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}$ , hiding) and (pk, sk)  $\leftarrow$  KeyGen(crs). For each challenge query, the challenger first samples  $(\sigma, r, \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [\rho]}) \leftarrow$  GenBits(crs) and gives r to  $\mathcal{A}$  before receiving a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$  chosen by  $\mathcal{A}$ . It then replies with  $\sigma$  and  $\{\pi_i\}_{i \in I}$ .

More precisely, in this experiment,

$$\operatorname{crs} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_{\rho} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\rho}}) \quad \text{and} \quad \operatorname{pk} = (g^{\mathbf{z}_1} h^{\hat{\mathbf{z}}_1}, \dots, g^{\mathbf{z}_{\rho}} h^{\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\rho}}),$$

where  $\mathbf{z}_i = (as_i + b_i)\mathbf{v}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{z}}_i = a\mathbf{e}_i$  for all  $i \in [\rho]$ . On each challenge query, the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{|N^2/4|}$  and computes

$$\sigma = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}$$
