 and  $\overline{t}_i = g^{s_i\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{e}_i$  and  $\overline{u}_i = (g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{z}_ih^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_i)^2$ ,

for all  $i \in [\rho]$ . The random bits  $r_i$  satisfy  $r_i = H(\overline{t}_i^2)$ , and the proofs  $\pi_i$  satisfy  $\pi_i = (\overline{t}_i, \overline{u}_i)$ .

- $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$ : Same as  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$ , except that the challenger computes  $(\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{sk}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_1(1^\lambda, 1^\rho)$  and uses  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathrm{and} \widetilde{\mathsf{sk}}$  instead of  $\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{pk}, \mathrm{and} \mathsf{sk}$ , respectively.
- Hyb<sub>2</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>1</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  instead of  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{|N^2/4|}^{\rho}$ .
- Hyb<sub>3</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>2</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{N}^{\rho}$ . It defines  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{N}$ .
- Hyb<sub>4</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>3</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ . Then it samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$ . Next, for each  $i \in [\rho]$ , it samples  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  such that  $r_i = H((g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}'_i})^2)$ . It uses the same rejection sampling procedure as in  $\mathcal{S}_2$ : namely, repeated sample  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  until finding one that satisfies the relation, and abort with output  $\bot$  if no such  $\hat{y}'_i$  is found after  $\lambda$  attempts. Finally it sets  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{N}$ . The remaining components are constructed as before.
- Hyb<sub>5</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>4</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\rho}$  after it receives the challenge set. In particular, on each query, after the challenger receives the set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , for each  $i \in I$ , it applies the same rejection sampling procedure as  $\mathcal{S}_2$  to sample  $\hat{y}'_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N$  such that  $r_i = H((g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h\hat{y}'_i)^2)$ . If  $i \notin I$ , then it samples  $r_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ . All remaining components are constructed as in Hyb<sub>4</sub>. This is the distribution in ExptHide[ $\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 1$ ].

**Lemma E.11.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_1(A)$ .

*Proof.* Since  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$  samples  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathsf{pk}}$ , and  $\widetilde{\mathsf{sk}}$  using the same procedure as Setup and KeyGen, the output distributions of hybrids  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$  are identically distributed.

<span id="page-76-1"></span>**Lemma E.12.** For all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_2(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* The only difference between  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$  is that the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y}$  uniformly at random from  $\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  instead of  $\mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}^{\rho}$  when answering challenge queries. Since the distributions  $\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor})$  and  $\mathsf{Uniform}(\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'})$  are statistically indistinguishable (see Eq. (E.1)), the claim follows by a union bound (since  $\rho = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and  $\mathcal{A}$  makes a polynomial number of queries).

<span id="page-76-2"></span>**Lemma E.13.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_3(A)$ .

*Proof.* The two distributions only differ in how  $\mathbf{y}$  is sampled. In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{y}$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\rho}$  while in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ , we sample  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\rho}$  and define  $\mathbf{y}$  so that  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{N}$ . These distributions are identical by the Chinese remainder theorem (since  $\gcd(p'q',N)=1$ ).

<span id="page-76-3"></span>**Lemma E.14.** If  $\mathcal{H}$  is a universal hash, then for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_4(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , the challenger first samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$ . In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ , the challenger then samples  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ , and sets

<span id="page-76-0"></span>
$$r_i = H((g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}_i'})^2) \tag{E.2}$$

for each  $i \in [\rho]$ . In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , the challenger first samples  $r_i \stackrel{\mathsf{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}$  and then samples  $\hat{y}_i' \stackrel{\mathsf{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\rho}$  such that Eq. (E.2) holds for each  $i \in [\rho]$ . First, all of the other components in Eq. (E.2) (i.e.,  $s_i$ ,  $\mathbf{v}$ , and  $\mathbf{y}'$ ) are *identically* distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ ). Thus, it suffices to show the following:

- The distribution of  $r_i$  in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$  is statistically close to uniform over  $\{0,1\}$ . This follows from the fact that  $\hat{y}'_i$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_N$ . This means that  $\hat{y}'_i$  is sampled from a distribution with at least  $\log N$  bits of min-entropy. Since  $\gcd(N,2)=1$ , the distribution of  $(g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{y}'_i})^2$  also has at least  $\log N$  bits of min-entropy over  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}$  (even after fixing  $s_i, \mathbf{v}, \mathbf{y}'$ ). Since  $\mathcal{H}$  is universal,  $1/N = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , we appeal to the the leftover hash lemma to conclude that  $r_i$  is statistically close to uniform over  $\{0,1\}$ . Since each  $\hat{y}'_i$  is sampled independently, each  $r_i$  is correspondingly independent and statistically close to uniform. By a union bound, we conclude that  $r \in \{0,1\}^\lambda$  is statistically close to uniform in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ . Thus, the distribution of r in the two experiments are statistically indistinguishable.
- With overwhelming probability, the sampling algorithm in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  does not abort. If this is the case, then in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , the distribution of  $\hat{y}_i'$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_N$  subject to Eq. (E.2) holding, which coincides with the distribution in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ . From the above analysis, we have that for  $\hat{y}_i' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ , the distribution of  $H((g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{v} h^{\hat{y}_i'})^2)$  is statistically close to uniform over  $\{0,1\}$ , and thus, will equal  $r_i$  with probability at least  $1/2 \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . The probability that the challenger fails to sample a  $\hat{y}_i'$  such that Eq. (E.2) holds is then  $1/2^\lambda \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Thus, the challenger in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  succeeds with overwhelming probability, and the claim follows.

**Lemma E.15.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_5(A)$ .

*Proof.* First, the challenger generates the common reference string crs and the public key pk identically in the two experiments. It suffices to argue that the challenger's response to the adversary's challenge query is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ . In particular, on each challenge query, after the adversary outputs a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , the challenger replies with a commitment  $\sigma = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$  and a collection of proofs  $\{\pi_i\}_{i\in I}$  where  $\pi_i = (\bar{t}_i, \overline{u}_i)$ . We show that the commitment  $\sigma$  and the group elements  $\bar{t}_i, \bar{u}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^*$  are identically distributed in the two experiments:

- In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ , the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\rho}$ . Since g generates a subgroup of order p'q' and  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$ , it follows that  $\sigma = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}} = g^{(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$ , and so  $\sigma$  is identically distributed in the two experiments.
- In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ , for all  $i \in I$ , the challenger samples  $\hat{y}_i' \in \mathbb{Z}_2$  conditioned on  $r_i = H\left((g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}_i'})^2\right)$ . Thus, the variables  $\hat{y}_i'$  for  $i \in I$  in the two experiments are identically distributed. In both experiments, the value  $\bar{t}_i$  satisfies  $\bar{t}_i = g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}_i'}$ , and since  $\mathbf{y}'$  and  $\hat{y}_i'$  are identically distributed in the two experiments (along with the remaining components  $s_i$ , and  $\mathbf{v}$ ), the value  $\bar{t}_i$  is also identically distributed in the two experiments.
- In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ ,  $\overline{u}_i = (g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{z}_ih^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_i)^2$ , where  $\mathbf{z}_i = (as_i + b_i)\mathbf{v}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{z}}_i = a\mathbf{e}_i$ . In particular, this means that  $\overline{u}_i = (g^{(as_i + b_i)(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{a\hat{y}_i'})^2$ . By construction, for all  $i \in I$ , all of the terms in the exponents are identically distributed in the two experiments.

The theorem now follows by a hybrid argument.

### <span id="page-77-0"></span>E.2 Dual-Mode Hidden-Bits Generator with Malicious Security from DCR

In this section, we describe our construction of a dual-mode hidden-bits generator with malicious security from the decisional composite residuosity (DCR) assumption from [Pai99]. This is an analog of Construction 5.9 from the QR assumption.

<span id="page-77-1"></span>Construction E.16 (Dual-Mode HBG with Malicious Security from DCR). Let  $\rho$  be the output length of the hidden-bits generator. Our construction relies on a similar set of building blocks as Construction 4.18:

- Let SampleModulus be a safe prime modulus sampler.
- Let  $\ell = 3\rho\lambda$  and define  $\mathcal{T}_{\lambda,\ell} := \{S \subseteq [\ell] : |S| = \lambda\}$  to be the set of all subsets of  $[\ell]$  that contains exactly  $\lambda$  elements. Let  $G : \{0,1\}^{\kappa} \to \mathcal{T}_{\lambda,\ell}^{\rho} \times \mathbb{Z}_N^{\rho\ell}$  be a PRG with seed length  $\kappa = \kappa(\lambda)$ . Here, N is the modulus output by SampleModulus. We refer to Construction 4.18 for a description of how to construct such a PRG.

We construct the dual-mode designated-verifier HBG with malicious security as follows:

- Setup $(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}, \text{mode}) \to \text{crs: Let } \ell' = \rho \ell$ . Sample  $(N, p, q) \leftarrow \text{SampleModulus}(1^{\lambda})$ . Let g be a generator of  $\mathbb{NR}_{2N}$  and h = 1 + N be the generator of  $\mathbb{H}$ . The setup algorithm samples a vector  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}^{\ell'}$ , scalars  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\ell'} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$  and sets  $\hat{\mathbf{w}}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$  for  $i \in [\ell']$  as follows:
  - if mode = hiding, set  $\hat{\mathbf{w}}_i \leftarrow \mathbf{e}_i$ , where  $\mathbf{e}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$  is the  $i^{\text{th}}$  basis vector.
  - If mode = binding, set  $\hat{\mathbf{w}}_i \leftarrow \mathbf{0}$ .

Finally, it samples a hash function  $H \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{H}$  where  $\mathcal{H}$  is a family of hash functions with domain  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}$  and range  $\{0,1\}$ . Output  $\mathsf{crs} = (N,g,h,H,g^\mathbf{v},g^{s_1\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}_1},\ldots,g^{s_{\ell'}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\mathbf{w}}_{\ell'}})$ .

- KeyGen(crs)  $\rightarrow$  (pk, sk): On input crs =  $(N, g, h, H, \overline{\mathbf{v}}, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\ell'})$ , sample  $a, b_1, \dots, b_{\ell'} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$  for each  $i \in [\ell']$ . Output pk =  $(\overline{\mathbf{v}}^{b_1} \overline{\mathbf{w}}_1^a, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{v}}^{b_{\ell'}} \overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\ell'}^a)$  and sk =  $(a, b_1, \dots, b_{\ell'})$ .
- GenBits(crs, pk)  $\to$   $(\sigma, r, \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [\rho]})$ : On input crs  $= (N, g, h, H, \overline{\mathbf{v}}, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\ell'})$  and pk  $= (\overline{\mathbf{z}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\ell'})$ , first check that  $\overline{\mathbf{z}}_i \in (\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*)^{\ell'}$  for all  $i \in [\ell']$  (and output  $\perp$  otherwise). Then, sample  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{N^2/4}^{\ell'}$  and compute for each  $i \in [\ell']$ :

$$\overline{c} \leftarrow \prod_{j \in [\ell']} \overline{v}_j^{y_j} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{t}_i \leftarrow \prod_{j \in [\ell']} \overline{w}_{i,j}^{y_j} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{u}_i \leftarrow \prod_{j \in [\ell']} (\overline{z}_{i,j}^2)^{y_j}.$$

Next, sample a PRG seed  $\mathbf{s} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  and compute  $(\hat{S}_1,\ldots,\hat{S}_{\rho},\boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(\mathbf{s})$  where  $\hat{S}_i \in \mathcal{T}_{\lambda,\ell}$  for all  $i \in [\rho]$  and  $\boldsymbol{\alpha} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\rho\ell}$ . Compute the shifted sets  $S_i \leftarrow \{j + \ell \cdot (i-1) \mid j \in \hat{S}_i\}$  for each  $i \in [\rho]$ . Finally, compute

$$r_i \leftarrow H\left(\prod_{j \in S_i} \overline{t}_j^{2\alpha_j}\right) \quad \text{ and } \quad \pi_i \leftarrow \{(j, \overline{t}_j, \overline{u}_j)\}_{j \in S_i}.$$

Output  $\sigma = (s, \overline{c}), r, \text{ and } \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [n]}.$ 

- Verify(crs, sk,  $\sigma$ , i,  $r_i$ ,  $\pi_i$ ): On input crs =  $(N, g, h, H, \overline{\mathbf{v}}, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{w}}_{\ell'})$ , sk =  $(a, b_1, \dots, b_{\ell'})$ ,  $\sigma$  =  $(\mathbf{s}, \overline{c})$ ,  $i \in [\rho]$ ,  $r_i \in \{0, 1\}$ , and  $\pi_i = \{(j, \overline{t}_j, \overline{u}_j)\}_{j \in S}$  for an implicitly-defined set  $S \subseteq [\ell']$ , the verification algorithm performs the following checks:
  - Compute  $(\hat{S}_1, \dots, \hat{S}_\rho, \boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(s)$  and the shifted set  $S_i \leftarrow \{j + \ell \cdot (i-1) \mid j \in \hat{S}_i\}$ . It checks that  $S = S_i$  and outputs 0 if not.
  - It checks that  $\overline{u}_j = (\overline{t}_j^a \overline{c}^{b_j})^2$  for all  $j \in S$ , and outputs 0 if not.
  - It checks that  $r_i = H(\prod_{j \in S} \bar{t}_j^{2\alpha_j})$  and outputs 0 if not.

If all checks pass, the verification algorithm outputs 1.

Correctness and security analysis. We state the correctness and security theorems for Construction 5.3 here, but defer the proofs to Appendix E.2.1.

<span id="page-78-0"></span>**Theorem E.17** (Correctness). Construction E.16 is correct.

<span id="page-78-2"></span>**Theorem E.18** (Succinctness). Construction E.16 is succinct.

<span id="page-78-3"></span>**Theorem E.19** (CRS Indistinguishability). Suppose the DCR assumption holds with respect to SampleModulus. Then, Construction E.16 satisfies CRS indistinguishability.

<span id="page-78-4"></span>**Theorem E.20** (Statistical Binding in Binding Mode). Construction E.16 satisfies statistical binding in binding mode.

<span id="page-78-1"></span>**Theorem E.21** (Statistical Simulation in Hiding Mode). Construction E.16 satisfies statistical simulation in hiding mode.

#### <span id="page-79-0"></span>E.2.1 Analysis of Construction E.16 (Dual-Mode (Malicious) HBG from DCR)

In this section, we give the proofs for the correctness and security theorems (Theorems E.17 to E.21) for the dual-mode hidden-bits generator with security against malicious verifiers from the DCR assumption (Construction E.16). The analysis is very similar to that of the basic scheme from DCR (Construction E.2).

**Proof of Theorem E.17 (Correctness).** Follows by an analogous argument as the proof of Theorem E.3.  $\Box$ 

**Proof of Theorem E.18 (Succinctness).** The commitment  $\sigma$  in Construction E.16 consists of a PRG seed  $s \in \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  where  $\kappa = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and an element of  $\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}$ , which has size  $2 \lceil \log N \rceil = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ .

**Proof of Theorem E.19 (CRS Indistinguishability).** Same as the proof of Theorem E.5.

**Proof of Theorem E.20 (Statistical Binding).** Follows by a similar argument as the proof of Theorem E.6.  $\Box$ 

**Proof of Theorem E.21 (Statistical Hiding).** We construct a simulator  $S = (S_1, S_2)$  as follows:

•  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}) \to (\operatorname{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{crs}})$ : Sample  $(N, p, q) \leftarrow \operatorname{SampleModulus}(1^{\lambda})$ , where p = 2p' + 1 and q = 2q' + 1. Let g be a generator of  $\mathbb{N}_{2N}$  and h = 1 + N be the generator of  $\mathbb{H}$ . Sample a vector  $\mathbf{v} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ , scalars  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\ell'} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}$ , and a hash function  $H \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{H}$ . Output

$$\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = \left(N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_{\ell'} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\ell'}}\right).$$

and  $\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}, p', q', s_1, \dots, s_{\ell'}).$ 

•  $S_2(\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}},\mathsf{pk},I,r_I) \to (\widetilde{\sigma},\{\widetilde{\pi}_i\}_{i\in I})$ : On input  $\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}} = (\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}},p',q',s_1,\ldots,s_{\ell'})$  where

$$\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = \left(N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \dots, g^{s_{\ell'} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\ell'}}\right),$$

a public key  $\mathsf{pk} = (\overline{\mathbf{z}}_1, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\ell'})$ , a set of indices  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , and a bitstring  $r_I \in \{0,1\}^{|I|}$ , the simulator does the following:

- 1. Check that  $\overline{\mathbf{z}}_i \in (\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*)^{\ell'}$  for all  $i \in [\ell']$ . Output  $\perp$  if this is not the case.
- 2. Sample a seed  $\mathbf{s} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  and compute  $(\hat{S}_1,\ldots,\hat{S}_{\rho},\boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(\mathbf{s})$ , where  $\boldsymbol{\alpha} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\rho\ell}$ . For each  $i \in I$ , it computes the shifted sets  $S_i \leftarrow \{j + \ell \cdot (i-1) \mid j \in \hat{S}_i\}$ .
- 3. Sample  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$ . Then, it samples a vector  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$  as follows:
  - For each  $i \in I$ , let  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$ . Then, sample  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  conditioned on  $r_i = H((g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}h^{\hat{\omega}_i})^2)$ . Specifically, repeatedly sample  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  until finding one that satisfies the relation. If no candidate is found after  $\lambda$  attempts, then abort and output  $\bot$ . After sampling  $\hat{\omega}_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  for each  $j \in S_i$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}'_j = \hat{\omega}_i$ .

- For all of the remaining indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ . Define  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Nv'q'}^{\ell'}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{N}$ .
- 4. Next, the simulator computes  $\widetilde{\sigma} = (\mathsf{s}, g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}), \ \overline{t}_j = g^{s_j\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{e}_j, \ \text{and} \ \overline{u}_j \leftarrow \prod_{k \in [\ell']} (\overline{z}_{j,k}^2)^{y_k}$  for all  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$ . It sets  $\widetilde{\pi}_i = \{(j, \overline{t}_j, \overline{u}_j)\}_{j \in S_i}$ .
- 5. Output  $\widetilde{\sigma}$  and  $\{\widetilde{\pi}_i\}_{i\in I}$ .

We now use a hybrid argument to show that  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A},0]$  and  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A},1]$  are statistically indistinguishable:

- Hyb<sub>0</sub>: This is the experiment ExptHide[ $\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 0$ ]. Namely, the challenger begins by sampling crs  $\leftarrow$  Setup( $1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho}$ , hiding), and gives crs to  $\mathcal{A}$ . The adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  replies with a public key pk. For each challenge query, the challenger samples  $(\sigma, r, \{\pi_i\}_{i \in [\rho]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{GenBits}(\mathsf{crs}, \mathsf{pk})$  and gives r to  $\mathcal{A}$  before receiving a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$  chosen by  $\mathcal{A}$ . It then replies with  $\sigma$  and  $\{\pi_i\}_{i \in I}$ .
- $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$ : This experiment is identical to  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$ , except that the challenger computes  $(\mathsf{st}_{\mathcal{S}}, \widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$  and uses  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$  in place of  $\mathsf{crs}$ . Everything else proceeds identically to  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$ .

Specifically, in this experiment, the challenger samples (N, p, q), H,  $\mathbf{v}$ ,  $s_1, \ldots, s_{\ell'}$  as specified by  $\mathcal{S}_1$  and sets  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}} = (N, g, h, H, g^{\mathbf{v}}, g^{s_1 \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_1}, \ldots, g^{s_{\ell'} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{e}_{\ell'}})$ . It gives  $\widetilde{\mathsf{crs}}$  to  $\mathcal{A}$  to receive a public key  $\mathsf{pk} = (\overline{\mathbf{z}}_1, \ldots, \overline{\mathbf{z}}_{\ell'})$ . On a challenge query, the challenger proceeds as follows:

- 1. Check that  $\overline{\mathbf{z}}_i \in (\mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*)^{\ell'}$  for all  $i \in [\ell']$ , and output  $\perp$  otherwise.
- 2. Sample  $s \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  and compute  $(\hat{S}_1,\ldots,\hat{S}_{\rho},\boldsymbol{\alpha}) \leftarrow G(s)$ . For each  $i \in [\rho]$ , let  $S_i \leftarrow \{j+\ell\cdot(i-1) \mid j\in\hat{S}_i\}$ .
- 3. Sample  $\mathbf{y} \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{\lfloor N^2/4 \rfloor}^{\ell'}$  and compute for each  $j \in [\ell']$ ,

$$\overline{c} \leftarrow g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{t}_j \leftarrow g^{s_j \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{v}} h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{e}_j} \quad \text{and} \quad \overline{u}_j \leftarrow \prod_{k \in [\ell']} (\overline{z}_{j,k}^2)^{y_k}.$$

- 4. For each  $i \in [\rho]$ , compute  $r_i \leftarrow H\left(\prod_{j \in S_i} \overline{t}_j^{2\alpha_j}\right)$  and  $\pi_i \leftarrow \{(j, \overline{t}_j, \overline{u}_j)\}_{j \in S_i}$ .
- 5. The challenger gives r to  $\mathcal{A}$  and receives a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ .
- 6. The challenger replies with  $\sigma=(\mathsf{s},\overline{c})$  and the set  $\{\pi_i\}_{i\in I}$ .
- Hyb<sub>2</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>1</sub>, except when responding to challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\ell'}$  instead of  $\mathbf{y} \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{|N^2/4|}^{\ell'}$ .
- Hyb<sub>3</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>2</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $\mathbf{y}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$ . It defines  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathbb{Z}_{Np'q'}^{\ell'}$  to be the vector where  $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{y}' \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\mathbf{y} = \hat{\mathbf{y}}' \pmod{N}$ .
- Hyb<sub>4</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>3</sub>, except when responding to challenge queries, the challenger samples s and  $\mathbf{y}'$  as in Hyb<sub>3</sub>. Next, for each  $i \in [\rho]$ , it samples  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ , and for  $j \in S_i$ , it samples  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}'_j = \hat{\omega}_i$ . For all of the remaining indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ .

- Hyb<sub>5</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>4</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger first samples  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ . Then, after sampling s and  $\mathbf{y}'$ , it computes for each  $i \in [\rho]$ ,  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$ . Then, it samples  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  conditioned on  $r_i = H((g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{\omega}_i})^2)$ . It uses the same rejection sampling procedure as in  $S_2$  to sample  $\hat{\omega}_i$ .
- Hyb<sub>6</sub>: Same as Hyb<sub>5</sub>, except when responding to the challenge queries, the challenger samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$  after it receives the challenge set. On each query, after the challenger receives the set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ , for each  $i \in I$ , it samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}'$  as follows:
  - For each  $i \in I$ , let  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$ . Then, sample  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  conditioned on  $r_i = H((g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{\omega}_i})^2)$  using the same rejection sampling procedure as in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ . After sampling  $\hat{\omega}_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_j \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  for each  $j \in S_i$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}'_j = \hat{\omega}_i$ .
  - For all of the remaining indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ , sample  $\hat{y}'_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ .

The remaining components are constructed as in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ . This is exactly the distribution in  $\mathsf{ExptHide}[\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{S}, 1]$ .

For an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ , we write  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i(\mathcal{A})$  to denote the output of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_i(\mathcal{A})$  with adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ . In the following, we show that the output distribution on each pair of adjacent experiments is statistically indistinguishable (or identically distributed).

**Lemma E.22.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_1(A)$ .

*Proof.* Since  $S_1(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$  samples  $\widetilde{crs}$  using the same procedure as  $\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\rho})$ , the output distributions of  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$  are identical.

**Lemma E.23.** For all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_2(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* Follows by the same argument as the proof of Lemma E.12.

**Lemma E.24.** For all adversaries A,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2(A) \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_3(A)$ .

*Proof.* Follows by the Chinese remainder theorem (as in the proof of Lemma E.13).  $\Box$ 

**Lemma E.25.** If G is a secure PRG, then for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_4(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ , the challenger samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}' \stackrel{\mathsf{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$  while in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , the challenger samples  $\hat{y}_j' \stackrel{\mathsf{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  subject to the constraint that  $\sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}_j' = \hat{\omega}_i$  where  $\hat{\omega}_i \stackrel{\mathsf{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  for  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in [\rho]$ . For the indices  $j \in [\ell'] \setminus \bigcup_{i \in I} S_i$ ,  $\hat{y}_j' \stackrel{\mathsf{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$ . These distributions are identical as long as there exists some  $j \in S_i$  where  $\alpha_j \in \mathbb{Z}_N^*$  for each  $i \in [\rho]$ . Since G is a secure PRG, this holds with overwhelming probability (by a similar argument as in the proof of Claim C.11).

**Lemma E.26.** If  $\mathcal{H}$  is a universal hash, then for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_5(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , except the challenger samples  $\hat{\mathbf{y}} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$  first in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$  while it samples  $r \in \{0,1\}^\rho$  first in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ . We show that these two distributions are statistically indistinguishable. In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , each challenge bit  $r_i$  satisfies

<span id="page-82-0"></span>
$$r_i = H\left(\prod_{j \in S_i} \bar{t}_j^{2\alpha_j}\right) = H\left(\prod_{j \in S_i} (g^{s_j \mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{v} h^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{e}_j)^{2\alpha_j}\right) = H((g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{v} h^{\hat{\omega}_i})^2), \tag{E.3}$$

where  $\omega_i = \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$  and  $\omega_i' = \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j \hat{y}_j' \pmod{N}$ , since g generates a group of order p'q' and h generates a group of order N. Now, in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_4$ , each  $\hat{\omega}_i$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_N$ , and  $r_i$  is derived from Eq. (E.3), while in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ ,  $r_i \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}$ , and  $\hat{\omega}_i$  is sampled uniformly from  $\mathbb{Z}_N$  subject to Eq. (E.3). Using an analogous argument to Lemma E.14, these two distributions are statistically indistinguishable.

**Lemma E.27.** If G is a secure PRG, then for all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5(\mathcal{A}) \overset{s}{\approx} \mathsf{Hyb}_6(\mathcal{A})$ .

*Proof.* The challenger samples  $\widetilde{\operatorname{crs}}$  identically in the two experiments, so  $N, g, h, \mathbf{v}, s_1, \ldots, s_{\ell'}$  are identically distributed in the two experiments. so it suffices to consider its responses to the challenge queries. In both experiments, on each query, the challenger starts by sending the adversary a random string  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\rho}$ , and the adversary replies with a set  $I \subseteq [\rho]$ . The challenger then replies with a commitment  $\sigma = (\mathsf{s}, \overline{c})$  and a set of proofs  $\{\pi_i\}_{i \in I}$ , where  $\pi_i = \{(j, \overline{t}_j, \overline{u}_j)\}_{j \in S_i}$ . We show that the challenger's responses are statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments. To this end, we define the following variables:

- For  $i \in [\rho]$ , let  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell}$  be the vector where  $\hat{y}_j^{(i)} = \hat{y}_{j+\ell\cdot(i-1)}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . In other words,  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^{\mathsf{T}} = [(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(1)})^{\mathsf{T}} \mid \cdots \mid (\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(\rho)})^{\mathsf{T}}] \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell'}$ .
- For  $i \in [\rho]$ , define  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} = (\alpha_1^{(i)}, \dots, \alpha_\ell^{(i)})^\top \in \mathbb{Z}_N^\ell$  as follows:

$$\alpha_j^{(i)} = \begin{cases} \alpha_{j+\ell \cdot (i-1)} & \text{if } j \in \hat{S}_i \\ 0 & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

We now consider the different components in the two experiments:

- The string r is independently and uniformly sampled from  $\{0,1\}^{\rho}$  in both experiments.
- The seed s is independently and uniformly sampled from  $\{0,1\}^{\kappa}$  in both experiments, so the seed s, the sets  $S_1, \ldots, S_{\rho}$ , and the vector  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}$  are identically distributed as well.
- The vector  $\mathbf{y}'$  is sampled uniformly from  $\mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}^{\ell'}$  in both experiments. Since g generates a group of order p'q', the commitment  $\overline{c} = g^{\mathbf{y}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}} = g^{(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{v}}$  is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ .
- For all  $i \in I$ , both experiments set  $\omega_i \leftarrow \sum_{j \in S_i} \alpha_j s_j \pmod{p'q'}$  and sample  $\hat{\omega}_i \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_N$  subject to  $r_i = H((g^{\omega_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{\omega}_i})^2)$ . This means that the vectors  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  for  $i \in I$  are identically distributed in the two experiments. Then, for  $j \in S_i$ , we have that  $\bar{t}_j = g^{s_i(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{v}h^{\hat{y}'_j}$ , so the components  $\bar{t}_j$  for  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$  are identically distributed.

It suffices to show that the remaining components  $\{\overline{u}_j\}_{j\in S_i}$  for  $i\in I$  are drawn from statistically indistinguishable distributions (from the view of the adversary). First, let

$$J = \{ j \in S_i \text{ for some } i \in I \mid j \in [\ell'] \}$$

be the set of indices that appear in some set  $S_i$  for  $i \in I$ . Since  $|S_i| = \lambda$  and the  $S_i$ 's are pairwise disjoint,  $|J| = \lambda |I| \le \lambda \rho = \ell/3$ .

It suffices to consider the case where  $\overline{\mathbf{z}}_j \in \mathbb{Z}_{N^2}^*$  for all  $j \in [\ell']$ . Otherwise, both experiments output  $\bot$ . This means  $\overline{z}_{j,k}^2 \in \mathbb{NR}_{2N} \times \mathbb{H}$ , and correspondingly, we can write  $\overline{z}_{j,k}^2 = g^{z_{j,k}} h^{\hat{z}_{j,k}}$  for some  $z_{j,k} \in \mathbb{Z}_{p'q'}$  and  $\hat{z}_{j,k} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . Now, for all  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$ , the challenger (in both experiments) computes  $\overline{u}_j$  as

$$\overline{u}_j = \prod_{k \in [\ell']} (\overline{z}_{j,k}^2)^{y_k} = \prod_{j \in [\ell']} g^{z_{j,k}y_k} h^{\hat{z}_{j,k}y_k} = g^{(\mathbf{y}')^\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{z}_j h^{(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}} \hat{\mathbf{z}}_j.$$

Since  $\mathbf{y}'$  is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ , it suffices to consider the distribution of  $\overline{u}_j$  in the  $\mathbb{H}$  subgroup, or equivalently, the distribution of  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{z}}_j$  over  $\mathbb{Z}_N$ . Let  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell' \times \ell'}$  be the matrix whose columns are  $\hat{\mathbf{z}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{z}}_{\ell'}$ . Let  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell' \times \lambda |I|}$  be the submatrix of  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$  formed by taking only the columns in  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$  indexed by the set J. In particular, the values of  $h^{(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}'} \in \mathbb{H}^{\lambda |I|}$  precisely coincide with the components in the  $\mathbb{H}$ -subgroup of  $\overline{u}_j$  for  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$ . Thus, it suffices to show that for these indices  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$ , the distributions of  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\lambda |I|}$  are statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments. First, for  $i \in [\rho]$ , let  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell \times \lambda |I|}$  be matrices such that

$$\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' = \left[ \begin{array}{c} \hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(1)} \ \vdots \ \hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(\rho)} \end{array} \right],$$

This means that

<span id="page-83-0"></span>
$$(\hat{\mathbf{y}}')^{\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}' = \sum_{i \in [\rho]} \left( (\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^{\mathsf{T}}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)} \right) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\lambda|I|}.$$
 (E.4)

By definition,  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}$  is a *fixed* matrix (determined by the CRS and the adversary's public key) and independent of  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}'$ . Since each  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is sampled independently, we can consider each term individually in this summation:

- If  $i \in I$ , then as argued above,  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is identically distributed in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ , and correspondingly, so is the product  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)}$ .
- If  $i \notin I$ , then the  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  in the two experiments are sampled from distinct distributions. In  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_N^\ell$  subject to  $\hat{\omega}_i = \sum_{j \in [\ell]} \alpha_j^{(i)} \hat{y}_j^{(i)}$ , while in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  is uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_N^\ell$ . By the Chinese remainder theorem, we can sample (and analyze) the  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $\mathbb{Z}_q$  components of  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)}$  independently.

Define  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_p^{(i)}$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_q^{(i)}$ ,  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_p^{(i)}$ , and  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_q^{(i)}$  as follows:

$$\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_p^{(i)} = \hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)} \pmod{p}$$
  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_p^{(i)} = \boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} \pmod{p}$   $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_a^{(i)} = \hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{(i)} \pmod{q}$   $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_q^{(i)} = \boldsymbol{\alpha}^{(i)} \pmod{q}$ .

By Claim C.11 (generalized to  $\mathbb{Z}_N$  via the Chinese remainder theorem), we have that with overwhelming probability,  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_p^{(i)} \notin \operatorname{span}(\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_p^{(i)})$  and  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_q^{(i)} \notin \operatorname{span}(\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_q^{(i)})$ . By Claim C.12, this means that the distribution of  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_p^{(i)} \pmod{p}$  in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  (where  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)} \pmod{p}$  is uniform subject to a linear constraint  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_p^{(i)} \notin \operatorname{span}(\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_p^{(i)})$ ) is statistically indistinguishable from its distribution in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$  (where  $\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)} \pmod{p}$  is uniform). By the same argument, the distributions of  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_q^{(i)} \pmod{p}$  in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_5$  and  $\mathsf{Hyb}_6$  are also statistically indistinguishable. By the Chinese remainder theorem and a union bound, this means that the product  $(\hat{\mathbf{y}}^{(i)})^\mathsf{T}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_q^{(i)} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\lambda|I|}$  is statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments.

Since every term in Eq. (E.4) is either statistically indistinguishable or identically distributed in the two experiments, we conclude that  $\hat{\mathbf{Z}}'\hat{\mathbf{y}}'$  is also statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments. Correspondingly, this means that the components  $\bar{u}_j$  for  $j \in S_i$  and  $i \in I$  are also statistically indistinguishable in the two experiments.

Since each consecutive pair of hybrid experiments is statistically indistinguishable (or identically distributed), the theorem follows.  $\Box$
